<p><b>Moscow</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">MOS</span>-koh</i></a>, <small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a> chiefly</small> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">MOS</span>-kow</i></a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Russian: <span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Москва</span></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">tr.</a></small> <span title="Russian-language text"><i lang="ru-Latn">Moskva</i></span>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" lang="ru-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[mɐskˈva]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/71/%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0.ogg" title="Москва.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Russia_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Russia by population">largest city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. The city stands on the <a href="/wiki/Moskva_(river)" title="Moskva (river)">Moskva River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Russia" title="Central Russia">Central Russia</a>, with a population estimated at 13.0 million residents within the city limits,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2021Census_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-2021Census-5">[5]</a></sup> over 17 million residents in the urban area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Urban-11">[11]</a></sup> and over 20 million residents in the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_metropolitan_area" title="Moscow metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Megapolis_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Megapolis-12">[12]</a></sup> The city covers an area of 2,511 square kilometers (970 sq mi), while the urban area covers 5,891 square kilometers (2,275 sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Urban-11">[11]</a></sup> and the metropolitan area covers over 26,000 square kilometers (10,000 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Megapolis_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Megapolis-12">[12]</a></sup> Moscow is among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">world's largest cities</a>; being the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_cities_by_population_within_city_limits" title="List of European cities by population within city limits">most populous city</a> entirely in Europe, the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_Europe" title="List of urban areas in Europe">urban</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe" title="List of metropolitan areas in Europe">metropolitan area</a> in Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Urban-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Megapolis_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Megapolis-12">[12]</a></sup> and the largest city by land area on the European continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planète_Énergies_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Planète_Énergies-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>First documented in 1147, Moscow grew to become a prosperous and powerful city that served as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy that bears its name</a>. When the Grand Duchy of Moscow evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>, Moscow remained the political and economic center for most of the Tsardom's history. When the Tsardom was reformed into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, the capital was moved from Moscow to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> diminishing the influence of the city. The capital was then moved back to Moscow following the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> and the city was brought back as the political center of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian SFSR</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Moscow remained the capital city of the contemporary and newly established Russian Federation.
</p><p>The northernmost and coldest <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> in the world, with a history that spans eight centuries, Moscow is governed as a <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal city</a> (since 1993)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> that serves as the political, economic, cultural, and scientific center of Russia and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>. As an <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">alpha world city</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Moscow has one of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">largest urban economies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The city is one of the fastest-growing tourist destinations in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and is one of Europe's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_international_visitors" title="List of cities by international visitors">most visited cities</a>. Moscow is home to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_number_of_billionaires" title="List of cities by number of billionaires">seventh-highest number of billionaires</a> of any city in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">Moscow International Business Center</a> is one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centers</a> in Europe and the world, and features the majority of <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Europe" title="List of tallest buildings in Europe">Europe's tallest skyscrapers</a>. Moscow was the host city of the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a>, and one of the host cities of the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>As the historic core of Russia, Moscow serves as the home of numerous Russian artists, scientists, and sports figures due to the presence of its various museums, academic and political institutions, and theaters. The city is home to several UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> and is well known for its display of <a href="/wiki/Russian_architecture" title="Russian architecture">Russian architecture</a>, particularly its historic <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>, and buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Basil's Cathedral">Saint Basil's Cathedral</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">Moscow Kremlin</a>, of which the latter serves as the seat of power of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Government of Russia</a>. Moscow is home to many <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Russia" title="List of companies of Russia">Russian companies</a> in numerous industries and is served by a comprehensive transit network, which includes <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Moscow_Airport_(disambiguation)#Commercial_passenger_and_cargo_traffic_airports" title="Moscow Airport (disambiguation)">four international airports</a>, ten railway terminals, a <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Moscow" title="Trams in Moscow">tram system</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Monorail" title="Moscow Monorail">monorail system</a>, and most notably the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a>, the busiest metro system in Europe, and one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> systems in the world. The city has over 40 percent of its territory covered by greenery, making it one of the greenest cities in Europe and the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planète_Énergies_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Planète_Énergies-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The name of the city is thought to be derived from the name of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River" title="Moskva River">Moskva River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smol_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smol-23">[23]</a></sup> Several theories of the origin of the name of the river have been proposed. Finno-Ugric <a href="/wiki/Volga_Finns" title="Volga Finns">Merya</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muroma" title="Muroma">Muroma</a> people, who were among the several pre-Slavic tribes which originally inhabited the area, called the river supposedly <i>Mustajoki</i>, in English: <i>Black river</i>. It has been suggested that the name of the city derives from this term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most linguistically well-grounded and widely accepted is from the Proto-Balto-Slavic root *<i>mŭzg</i>-/<i>muzg</i>- from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a> *<i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:nowrap;" title="Proto-Indo-European language"><span lang="ine">meu</span></span></i>- "wet",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smol_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Smol-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trubach_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trubach-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> so the name <i>Moskva</i> might signify a river at a wetland or a marsh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognates</a> include <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">музга</span>, <span title="Russian-language text"><i lang="ru-Latn">muzga</i></span> "pool, puddle", <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>: <i lang="lt">mazgoti</i> and <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">mazgāt</i> "to wash", <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a>: <span lang="sa">májjati</span> "to drown", <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">mergō</i> "to dip, immerse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trubach_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trubach-26">[26]</a></sup> In many Slavic countries Moskov is a surname, most common in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, Russia, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Additionally, there are similarly named places in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> like <a href="/wiki/Mozgawa" title="Mozgawa">Mozgawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smol_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Smol-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trubach_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Trubach-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>The original <a href="/wiki/Old_East_Slavic" title="Old East Slavic">Old Russian</a> form of the name is reconstructed as *<span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><span lang="orv">Москы</span></span>, *<span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><i lang="orv-Latn">Mosky</i></span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smol_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-Smol-23">[23]</a></sup> hence it was one of a few Slavic <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Category:Proto-Slavic_v-stem_nouns" title="wikt:Category:Proto-Slavic v-stem nouns"><i>ū</i>-stem nouns</a>. As with other nouns of that declension, it had been undergoing a morphological transformation at the early stage of the development of the language, as a result, the first written mentions in the 12th century were <span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><span lang="orv">Московь</span></span>, <span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><i lang="orv-Latn">Moskovĭ</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">accusative case</a>), <span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><span lang="orv">Москви</span></span>, <span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><i lang="orv-Latn">Moskvi</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Locative_case" title="Locative case">locative case</a>), <span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><span lang="orv">Москвe/Москвѣ</span></span>, <span title="Old East Slavic-language text"><i lang="orv-Latn">Moskve/Moskvě</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive case</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smol_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-Smol-23">[23]</a></sup> From the latter forms came to the modern Russian name <span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Москва</span></span>, <span title="Russian-language text"><i lang="ru-Latn">Moskva</i></span>, which is a result of <a href="/wiki/Morphological_leveling" title="Morphological leveling">morphological generalization</a> with the numerous Slavic <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Category:Proto-Slavic_hard_a-stem_nouns" title="wikt:Category:Proto-Slavic hard a-stem nouns"><i>ā</i>-stem nouns</a>.
</p><p>However, the form <i>Moskovĭ</i> has left some traces in many other languages, such as English: <span lang="en">Moscow</span>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Moskau</i>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Moscou</i>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>: <span title="Georgian-language text"><span lang="ka" style="font-style: normal;">მოსკოვი</span></span>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">Maskava</i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span title="Ottoman Turkish (1500-1928)-language text"><i lang="ota-Latn">Moskov</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Bashkir_language" title="Bashkir language">Bashkir</a>: <span lang="ba">Мәскәү</span>, <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a>: <i lang="tt-Latn">Mäskäw</i>, <span title="Chuvash-language text"><i lang="cv-Latn">Muskav</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Moscovo</i>, <span title="Kazakh-language text"><i lang="kk-Latn">Mäskew</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> <i>Moskova</i>, <a href="/wiki/Erzya_language" title="Erzya language">Erzya</a> <i>Moskov</i>, <a href="/wiki/Chuvash_language" title="Chuvash language">Chuvash</a>: <span lang="cv">Мускав</span>, <span title="Chuvash-language text"><i lang="cv-Latn">Muskav</i></span>, etc. In a similar manner the Latin name <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Moscovia</i></span> has been formed, later it became a colloquial name for Russia used in Western Europe in the 16th–17th centuries. From it as well came English <i>Muscovy</i> and <i>muscovite</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various other theories (of <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Caucasus" title="Languages of the Caucasus">Caucasic</a> origins), having little or no scientific ground, are now largely rejected by contemporary linguists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasmer_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-Vasmer-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smol_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-Smol-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_names">Other names</span></h3>
<p>Moscow has acquired several <a href="/wiki/Epithet" title="Epithet">epithets</a>, most referring to its size and preeminent status within the nation: The <i><a href="/wiki/Moscow,_third_Rome" title="Moscow, third Rome">Third Rome</a></i> (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Третий Рим</span></span>), the <i>Whitestone One</i> (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Белокаменная</span></span>), the <i>First Throne</i> (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Первопрестольная</span></span>), the <i>Forty Soroks</i> (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Сорок Сороков</span></span>) ("sorok" meaning both "forty, a great many" and "a district or parish" in <a href="/wiki/Old_East_Slavic" title="Old East Slavic">Old Russian</a>). Moscow is also one of the twelve <a href="/wiki/Hero_City_(Soviet_Union)" title="Hero City (Soviet Union)">Hero Cities</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> for a Moscow resident is "<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">москвич</span></span>" (<i>moskvich</i>) for male or "<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">москвич</span></span>ка" (<i>moskvichka</i>) for female, rendered in English as <i>Muscovite</i>. The name "Moscow" is abbreviated "MSK" (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">МСК</span></span> in Russian).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Moscow" title="History of Moscow">History of Moscow</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Moscow" title="Timeline of Moscow">Timeline of Moscow</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3>
<p>Archaeological digs show that the site of today's Moscow and the surrounding area have been inhabited since time immemorial. Among the earliest finds are relics of the Lyalovo culture, which experts assign to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period, the last phase of the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>They confirm that the first inhabitants of the area were hunters and gatherers. Around 950 AD, two Slavic tribes, <a href="/wiki/Vyatichi" title="Vyatichi">Vyatichi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krivichi" title="Krivichi">Krivichi</a>, settled here. Possibly the Vyatichi formed the core of Moscow's indigenous population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Early_history_.281147.E2.80.931284.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history_(1147–1284)">Early history (1147–1284)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Vladimir-Suzdal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="2301" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png/190px-Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png/285px-Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png/380px-Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kyivan_Rus%27_1220-1240.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Vladimir-Suzdal</a>, a principality on the northeastern periphery of <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a>, grew into the Grand Duchy of Moscow.</div></div></div>
<p>The first known reference to Moscow dates from 1147 as a meeting place of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuri_Dolgoruky" title="Yuri Dolgoruky">Yuri Dolgoruky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_Olgovich" title="Sviatoslav Olgovich">Sviatoslav Olgovich</a>. At the time it was a minor town on the western border of Vladimir-Suzdal Principality. The chronicle says, "Come, my brother, to Moskov" (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Приди ко мне, брате, в Москов</span></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1156, Knyaz <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Dolgorukiy" title="Yuri Dolgorukiy">Yuri Dolgorukiy</a> fortified the town with a timber fence and a moat. In the course of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'">Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'</a>, the Mongols under <a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a> burned the city to the ground and killed its inhabitants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The timber fort <i>na Moskvě</i> "on the Moscow River" was inherited by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_of_Moscow" title="Daniel of Moscow">Daniel</a>, the youngest son of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky" title="Alexander Nevsky">Alexander Nevsky</a>, in the 1260s, at the time considered the least valuable of his father's possessions.
Daniel was still a child at the time, and the big fort was governed by <span title="Russian-language romanization"><i lang="ru-Latn">tiuns</i></span> (deputies), appointed by Daniel's paternal uncle, <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_of_Tver" title="Yaroslav of Tver">Yaroslav of Tver</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Daniel came of age in the 1270s and became involved in the power struggles of the principality with lasting success, siding with his brother <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_of_Pereslavl" title="Dmitry of Pereslavl">Dmitry</a> in his bid for the rule of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novgorod" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a>. From 1283 he acted as the ruler of an independent principality alongside Dmitry, who became <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Vladimir" title="Grand Duke of Vladimir">Grand Duke of Vladimir</a>.
Daniel has been credited with founding the first Moscow monasteries, dedicated to the Lord's Epiphany and to Saint Daniel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Grand_Duchy_.281283.E2.80.931547.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Duchy_(1283–1547)">Grand Duchy (1283–1547)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a></div>
<table class="graytable" style="text-align:center">
<caption>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width:33%;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kremlenagrad.jpg"><img alt="Kremlenagrad.jpg" data-file-height="2098" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kremlenagrad.jpg/350px-Kremlenagrad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kremlenagrad.jpg/525px-Kremlenagrad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kremlenagrad.jpg/700px-Kremlenagrad.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
</td>
<td style="width:33%;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10,_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg"><img alt="Facial Chronicle - b.10, p.049 - Tokhtamysh at Moscow.jpg" data-file-height="796" data-file-width="438" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg/150px-Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg/225px-Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg/300px-Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.049_-_Tokhtamysh_at_Moscow.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
</td>
<td style="width:33%;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg"><img alt="Mikhail Feodorovich Izbranie.jpg" data-file-height="967" data-file-width="1064" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg/310px-Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg/465px-Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg/620px-Mikhail_Feodorovich_Izbranie.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">Moscow Kremlin</a> in the late 16th century
</td>
<td>The <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Moscow_(1382)" title="Siege of Moscow (1382)">Siege of Moscow</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Daniel ruled Moscow as Grand Duke until 1303 and established it as a prosperous city that would eclipse its parent principality of Vladimir by the 1320s.
</p><p>On the right bank of the Moskva River, at a distance of eight kilometres (5 mi) from the Kremlin, not later than in 1282, Daniel founded the first monastery with the wooden church of St. Daniel-Stylite, which is now the Danilov Monastery. Daniel died in 1303, at the age of 42. Before his death, he became a monk and, according to his will, was buried in the cemetery of the St. Daniel Monastery.
</p><p>Moscow was quite stable and prosperous for many years and attracted a large number of refugees from across Russia. The Rurikids maintained large landholdings by practicing <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">primogeniture</a>, whereby all land was passed to the eldest sons, rather than dividing it up among all sons. By 1304, <a href="/wiki/Yury_of_Moscow" title="Yury of Moscow">Yury of Moscow</a> contested with <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_of_Tver" title="Mikhail of Tver">Mikhail of Tver</a> for the throne of the principality of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir,_Russia" title="Vladimir, Russia">Vladimir</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_I_of_Russia" title="Ivan I of Russia">Ivan I</a> eventually defeated <a href="/wiki/Tver" title="Tver">Tver</a> to become the sole collector of taxes for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> rulers, making Moscow the capital of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Vladimir-Suzdal</a>. By paying high tribute, Ivan won an important concession from the <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khan</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg/220px-Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg/330px-Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg/440px-Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andronikov_Monastery_18.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spassky Cathedral (Moscow's oldest extant building), built c. 1357</div></div></div>
<p>While the Khan of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> initially attempted to limit Moscow's influence, when the growth of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a> began to threaten all of Russia, the Khan strengthened Moscow to counterbalance Lithuania, allowing it to become one of the most powerful cities in Russia. In 1380, prince <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Donskoy" title="Dmitry Donskoy">Dmitry Donskoy</a> of Moscow led a united Russian army to an important victory over the Mongols in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kulikovo" title="Battle of Kulikovo">Battle of Kulikovo</a>. Afterward, Moscow took the leading role in liberating Russia from Mongol domination. In 1480, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_III_of_Russia" title="Ivan III of Russia">Ivan III</a> had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_standing_on_the_Ugra_river" title="Great standing on the Ugra river">finally broken the Russians free</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatar" title="Tatar">Tatar</a> control, and Moscow became the capital of an empire that would eventually encompass all of Russia and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, and parts of many other lands.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BD%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%8F.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="255" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BD%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%8F.jpg/255px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BD%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%8F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BD%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%8F.jpg/340px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BD%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%8F.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BD%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%8F.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Spasskaya_Tower" title="Spasskaya Tower">Spasskaya Tower</a>, built in 1491</div></div></div>
<p>In 1462 Ivan III, (1440–1505) became Grand Prince of Moscow (then part of the medieval Muscovy state). He began fighting the Tatars, enlarged the territory of Muscovy, and enriched his capital city. By 1500 it had a population of 100,000 and was one of the largest cities in the world. He conquered the far larger principality of Novgorod to the north, which had been allied to the hostile Lithuanians. Thus he enlarged the territory sevenfold, from 430,000 to 2,800,000 square kilometres (170,000 to 1,080,000 square miles). He took control of the ancient "<a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Chronicle" title="Novgorod Chronicle">Novgorod Chronicle</a>" and made it a propaganda vehicle for his regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>The original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">Moscow Kremlin</a> was built in the 14th century. It was reconstructed by Ivan, who in the 1480s invited architects from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renaissance_Italy" title="Renaissance Italy">Renaissance Italy</a>, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrus_Antonius_Solarius" title="Petrus Antonius Solarius">Petrus Antonius Solarius</a>, who designed the new Kremlin wall and its towers, and <a href="/wiki/Marco_Ruffo" title="Marco Ruffo">Marco Ruffo</a> who designed the new palace for the prince. The Kremlin walls as they now appear are those designed by Solarius, completed in 1495. The Kremlin's Great Bell Tower was built in 1505–08 and augmented to its present height in 1600.
</p><p>A trading settlement, or <i>posad</i>, grew up to the east of the Kremlin, in the area known as <i>Zaradye</i> (Зарядье). In the time of Ivan III, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>, originally named the Hollow Field (Полое поле) appeared.
</p><p>In 1508–1516, the Italian architect <a href="/wiki/Aloisio_the_New" title="Aloisio the New">Aleviz Fryazin (Novy)</a> arranged for the construction of a moat in front of the eastern wall, which would connect the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River" title="Moskva River">Moskva</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neglinnaya_River" title="Neglinnaya River">Neglinnaya</a> and be filled in with water from Neglinnaya. This moat, known as the Alevizov moat and having a length of 541 metres (1,775 feet), width of 36 metres (118 feet), and a depth of 9.5 to 13 metres (31–43 feet) was lined with limestone and, in 1533, fenced on both sides with low, four-metre-thick (13-foot) cogged-brick walls.<span class="anchor" id="Tsardom"></span>
</p>
<h3><span id="Tsardom_.281547.E2.80.931721.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tsardom_(1547–1721)">Tsardom (1547–1721)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2065" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg/220px-Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg/330px-Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg/440px-Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_StBasilCathedral_d28.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Basil's Cathedral">Saint Basil's Cathedral</a>, built in 1561</div></div></div>
<p>In the 16th and 17th centuries, the three circular defenses were built: <a href="/wiki/Kitay-gorod" title="Kitay-gorod">Kitay-gorod</a> (Китай-город), the White City (Белый город) and the Earthen City (Земляной город). However, in 1547, two fires destroyed much of the town, and in 1571 the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> <a href="/wiki/Russo-Crimean_Wars" title="Russo-Crimean Wars">captured Moscow</a>, burning everything except the Kremlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The annals record that only 30,000 of 200,000 inhabitants survived.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8F._%D0%92%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%85%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B5_XVII_%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0._1922,_%D0%B1%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5,_%D1%83%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C,_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C,_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%88.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="2035" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/%D0%A0%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8F._%D0%92%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%85%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B5_XVII_%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0._1922%2C_%D0%B1%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%2C_%D1%83%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%88.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/%D0%A0%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8F._%D0%92%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%85%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B5_XVII_%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0._1922%2C_%D0%B1%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%2C_%D1%83%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%88.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/%D0%A0%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8F._%D0%92%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%85%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B5_XVII_%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0._1922%2C_%D0%B1%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%2C_%D1%83%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%88.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8F._%D0%92%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%85%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%8F%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BB%D1%8C_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B5_XVII_%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0._1922,_%D0%B1%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5,_%D1%83%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C,_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C,_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%88.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of 17th-century Moscow (1922 drawing by <a href="/wiki/Apollinary_Vasnetsov" title="Apollinary Vasnetsov">Apollinary Vasnetsov</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Crimea" title="Khanate of Crimea">Crimean Tatars</a> attacked again in 1591, but this time were held back by new defense walls, built between 1584 and 1591 by a craftsman named <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Kon" title="Fyodor Kon">Fyodor Kon</a>. In 1592, an outer earth rampart with 50 towers was erected around the city, including an area on the right bank of the Moscow River. As an outermost line of defense, a chain of strongly fortified monasteries was established beyond the ramparts to the south and east, principally the <a href="/wiki/Novodevichy_Convent" title="Novodevichy Convent">Novodevichy Convent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donskoy_Monastery" title="Donskoy Monastery">Donskoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danilov_Monastery" title="Danilov Monastery">Danilov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simonov_Monastery" title="Simonov Monastery">Simonov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novospassky_Monastery" title="Novospassky Monastery">Novospasskiy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andronikov_Monastery" title="Andronikov Monastery">Andronikov</a> monasteries, most of which now house museums. From its ramparts, the city became poetically known as <i>Bielokamennaya</i>, the "White-Walled." The city's limits as marked by the ramparts built in 1592 are now marked by the <a href="/wiki/Garden_Ring" title="Garden Ring">Garden Ring</a>.
</p><p>Three square gates existed on the eastern side of the Kremlin wall, which in the 17th century, were known as Konstantino-Eleninsky, Spassky, Nikolsky (owing their names to the icons of Constantine and Helen, the Saviour and St. Nicholas that hung over them). The last two were directly opposite the Red Square, while the Konstantino-Elenensky gate was located behind Saint Basil's Cathedral.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5100" data-file-width="6600" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG/220px-Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG/330px-Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG/440px-Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Polish_plan_of_Moscow_1610.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Sigismundian" Plan of Moscow (1610), named after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_of_Poland" title="Sigismund III of Poland">Sigismund III of Poland</a>, is the last city plan compiled before the destruction of the city in 1612 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Muscovite_War_(1605%E2%80%931618)" title="Polish–Muscovite War (1605–1618)">retreating Polish troops</a> and subsequent changes to the street network. Orientation: north is at the right, west at the top</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1601%E2%80%9303" title="Russian famine of 1601–03">Russian famine of 1601–03</a> killed perhaps 100,000 in Moscow. From 1610 through 1612, troops of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> occupied Moscow, as its ruler <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa" title="Sigismund III Vasa">Sigismund III</a> tried to take the Russian throne. In 1612, the people of <a href="/wiki/Nizhny_Novgorod" title="Nizhny Novgorod">Nizhny Novgorod</a> and other Russian cities conducted by prince <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Pozharsky" title="Dmitry Pozharsky">Dmitry Pozharsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuzma_Minin" title="Kuzma Minin">Kuzma Minin</a> rose against the Polish occupants, <a href="/wiki/Time_of_Troubles" title="Time of Troubles">besieged the Kremlin, and expelled them</a>. In 1613, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zemsky_sobor" title="Zemsky sobor">Zemsky sobor</a> elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Russia" title="Michael I of Russia">Michael Romanov</a> tsar, establishing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanov_dynasty" title="Romanov dynasty">Romanov dynasty</a>. The 17th century was rich in popular risings, such as the liberation of Moscow from the Polish–Lithuanian invaders (1612), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_Riot" title="Salt Riot">Salt Riot</a> (1648), the <a href="/wiki/Copper_Riot" title="Copper Riot">Copper Riot</a> (1662), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Uprising_of_1682" title="Moscow Uprising of 1682">Moscow Uprising of 1682</a>.
</p><p>During the first half of the 17th century, the population of Moscow doubled from roughly 100,000 to 200,000. It expanded beyond its ramparts in the later 17th century. It is estimated, that in the middle of the 17th century, 20% of Moscow suburb's inhabitants were from the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, practically all of them being driven from their homeland to Moscow by Muscovite invaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> By 1682, there were 692 households established north of the ramparts, by <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> abducted from their hometowns in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Polish_War_(1654%E2%80%931667)" title="Russo-Polish War (1654–1667)">Russo-Polish War (1654–1667)</a>. These new outskirts of the city came to be known as the <i>Meshchanskaya <a href="/wiki/Sloboda" title="Sloboda">sloboda</a></i>, after Ruthenian <i>meshchane</i> "town people". The term <i>meshchane</i> (мещане) acquired pejorative connotations in 18th-century Russia and today means "petty bourgeois" or "narrow-minded philistine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>The entire city of the late 17th century, including the <a href="/wiki/Sloboda" title="Sloboda">slobodas</a> that grew up outside the city ramparts, are contained within what is today Moscow's <a href="/wiki/Central_Administrative_Okrug" title="Central Administrative Okrug">Central Administrative Okrug</a>.
</p><p>Numerous disasters befell the city. The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">plague</a> epidemics ravaged Moscow in 1570–1571, 1592 and 1654–1656.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The plague killed upwards of 80% of the people in 1654–55. Fires burned out much of the wooden city in 1626 and 1648.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
In 1712 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Russia" title="Peter I of Russia">Peter the Great</a> moved his government to the newly built <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> on the Baltic coast. Moscow ceased to be Russia's capital, except for a brief period from 1728 to 1732 under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Privy_Council" title="Supreme Privy Council">Supreme Privy Council</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Empire_.281721.E2.80.931917.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Empire_(1721–1917)">Empire (1721–1917)</span></h3>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1969px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image"
