<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_landmarks">Parks and landmarks</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Moscow_tourist_attractions" title="List of Moscow tourist attractions">List of Moscow tourist attractions</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1508px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg" title="Red Square is a World Heritage Site."><img alt="" data-file-height="1452" data-file-width="8773" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg/1500px-Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg/2250px-Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg/3000px-Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg 2x" width="1500"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_360_Red_Square_edit.jpg" title="File:Panorama 360 Red Square edit.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a> is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>There are 96 parks and 18 gardens in Moscow, including four <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a>. There are 450 square kilometres (170 sq mi) of green zones besides 100 square kilometres (39 sq mi) of forests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-109">[109]</a></sup> Moscow is a very green city, if compared to other cities of comparable size in Western Europe and North America; this is partly due to a history of having green "yards" with trees and grass, between residential buildings. There are on average 27 square meters (290 sq ft) of parks per person in Moscow compared with 6 for <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, 7.5 in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and 8.6 in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greendress_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-greendress-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2489" data-file-width="4425" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg/220px-Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg/330px-Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg/440px-Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Gorky_Park_main_portal_08-2016_img1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gorky_Park_(Moscow)" title="Gorky Park (Moscow)">Gorky Park</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gorky_Park_(Moscow)" title="Gorky Park (Moscow)">Gorky Park</a> (officially the <a href="/wiki/Gorky_Park_(Moscow)" title="Gorky Park (Moscow)">Central Park of Culture and Rest</a> named after <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Gorky" title="Maxim Gorky">Maxim Gorky</a>), was founded in 1928. The main part (689,000 square metres or 170 acres)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greendress_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-greendress-110">[110]</a></sup> along the Moskva river contains <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Architectural_glossary#Estrade" title="Architectural glossary">estrades</a>, children's attractions (including the <i>Observation Wheel</i> water ponds with boats and water bicycles), dancing, tennis courts and other sports facilities. It borders the <a href="/wiki/Neskuchny_Garden" title="Neskuchny Garden">Neskuchny Garden</a> (408,000 square metres or 101 acres), the oldest park in Moscow and a former imperial residence, created as a result of the integration of three estates in the 18th century. The Garden features the Green Theater, one of the largest open amphitheaters in Europe, able to hold up to 15 thousand people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Several parks include a section known as a "Park of Culture and Rest", sometimes alongside a much wilder area (this includes parks such as Izmaylovsky, Fili and Sokolniki). Some parks are designated as Forest Parks (lesopark).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Island_of_Dreams2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Island_of_Dreams2.jpg/220px-Island_of_Dreams2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Island_of_Dreams2.jpg/330px-Island_of_Dreams2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Island_of_Dreams2.jpg/440px-Island_of_Dreams2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Island_of_Dreams2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dream_Island_(amusement_park)" title="Dream Island (amusement park)">Dream Island</a>, the largest indoor theme park in Europe</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Izmaylovsky_Park" title="Izmaylovsky Park">Izmaylovsky Park</a>, created in 1931, is one of the largest urban parks in the world along with <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Park" title="Richmond Park">Richmond Park</a> in London. Its area of 15.34 square kilometres (5.92 sq mi) is six times greater than that of <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a> in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greendress_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-greendress-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bauman_Garden_(Moscow)" title="Bauman Garden (Moscow)">Bauman  Garden</a>, officially founded in 1920 and renamed in 1922 after the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Bauman" title="Nikolay Bauman">Nikolay Bauman</a>, is one of the oldest parks in Moscow. It is standing on the site of the former <a href="/wiki/House_of_Golitsyn" title="House of Golitsyn">Golitsyn</a> estate and eighteenth-century public garden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVostryshev,_Shokarev201157—58_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVostryshev,_Shokarev201157—58-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg/220px-Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg/330px-Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg/440px-Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novodevichy_Convent_Night.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Novodevichy_Convent" title="Novodevichy Convent">Novodevichy Convent</a> is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Sokolniki_Park" title="Sokolniki Park">Sokolniki Park</a>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Falcon" title="Falcon">falcon</a> hunting that occurred there in the past, is one of the oldest parks in Moscow and has an area of 6 square kilometres (2.3 sq mi). A central circle with a large fountain is surrounded by birch, maple, and elm tree alleys. A labyrinth composed of green paths lies beyond the park's ponds.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Losiny_Ostrov_National_Park" title="Losiny Ostrov National Park">Losiny Ostrov National Park</a> ("Elk Island" National Park), with a total area of more than 116 square kilometres (45 sq mi), borders Sokolniki Park and was Russia's first national park. It is quite wild, and is also known as the "city taiga" – elk can be seen there.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_(19.08.2018).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6217" data-file-width="4782" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%2819.08.2018%29.jpg/170px-%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%2819.08.2018%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%2819.08.2018%29.jpg/255px-%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%2819.08.2018%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%2819.08.2018%29.jpg/340px-%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%2819.08.2018%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_(19.08.2018).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Church of Ascension in <a href="/wiki/Kolomenskoye" title="Kolomenskoye">Kolomenskoye</a> is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Tsytsin Main <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Botanical_Garden_of_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Moscow Botanical Garden of Academy of Sciences">Botanical Garden of Academy of Sciences</a>, founded in 1945 is the largest in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> It covers the territory of 3.61 square kilometres (1.39 sq mi) bordering the All-Russia Exhibition Center and contains a live exhibition of more than 20 thousand species of plants from around the world, as well as a lab for scientific research. It contains a rosarium with 20 thousand rose bushes, a dendrarium, and an oak forest, with the average age of trees exceeding 100 years. There is a greenhouse taking up more than 5,000 square metres (53,820 square feet) of land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greendress_110-3"><a href="#cite_note-greendress-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>The All-Russian Exhibition Center (Всероссийский выставочный центр), formerly known as the All-Union Agricultural Exhibition (VSKhV) and later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VDNKh_(Russia)" title="VDNKh (Russia)">Exhibition of Achievements of the National Economy</a> (VDNKh), though officially named a "permanent trade show", is one of the most prominent examples of Stalinist-era monumental architecture. Among the large spans of a recreational park, areas are scores of elaborate pavilions, each representing either a branch of Soviet industry and science or a USSR republic. Even though during the 1990s it was, and for some part still is, misused as a gigantic shopping center (most of the pavilions are rented out for small businesses), it still retains the bulk of its architectural landmarks, including two monumental fountains (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Stone_Flower_Fountain" title="The Stone Flower Fountain">Stone Flower</a></i> and <i>Friendship of Nations</i>) and a 360 degrees panoramic cinema. In 2014 the park returned to the name Exhibition of Achievements of National Economy, and in the same year, huge renovation works had been started.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Lilac Park</i>, founded in 1958, has a permanent sculpture display and a large rosarium. Moscow has always been a popular destination for tourists. Some of the more famous attractions include the city's UNESCO World Heritage Site, Moscow Kremlin and Red Square,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> which was built between the 14th and 17th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kolomenskoye#The_White_Column_of_Kolomenskoye" title="Kolomenskoye">Church of the Ascension</a> at Kolomenskoye, which dates from 1532, is also a UNESCO World Heritage Site and another popular attraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>Near the <a href="/wiki/Tretyakov_Gallery" title="Tretyakov Gallery">new Tretyakov Gallery</a> there is a sculpture garden, Museon, often called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_graveyard_of_fallen_monuments" title="The graveyard of fallen monuments">the graveyard of fallen monuments</a>" that displays statues of the former Soviet Union that were removed from their place after its dissolution.
</p><p>Other attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Zoo" title="Moscow Zoo">Moscow Zoo</a>, a zoological garden in two sections (the valleys of two streams) linked by a bridge, with nearly a thousand species and more than 6,500 specimens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moszoo_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-moszoo-118">[118]</a></sup> Each year, the zoo attracts more than 1.2 million visitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moszoo_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-moszoo-118">[118]</a></sup> Many of Moscow's parks and landscaped gardens are protected natural environments.
</p>
<table class="graytable" style="text-align:center">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_rings">Moscow rings</span></h2>
<p>Moscow's road system is centered roughly on the Kremlin at the heart of the city. From there, roads generally span outwards to intersect with a sequence of circular roads ("rings").
</p>
<ol><li>The first and innermost major ring, Bulvarnoye Koltso (<a href="/wiki/Boulevard_Ring" title="Boulevard Ring">Boulevard Ring</a>), was built at the former location of the 16th-century city wall around what used to be called <a href="/wiki/Bely_Gorod" title="Bely Gorod">Bely Gorod</a> (White Town).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-golden-ring_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-golden-ring-119">[119]</a></sup> The Bulvarnoye Koltso is technically not a ring; it does not form a complete circle, but instead a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horseshoe-shaped" title="Horseshoe-shaped">horseshoe-shaped</a> arc that begins at the Cathedral of Christ the Savior and ends at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yauza_River" title="Yauza River">Yauza River</a>.</li>
<li>The second primary ring, located outside the Boulevard Ring, is the Sadovoye Koltso (<a href="/wiki/Garden_Ring" title="Garden Ring">Garden Ring</a>). Like the Boulevard Ring, the Garden Ring follows the path of a 16th-century wall that used to encompass part of Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-golden-ring_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-golden-ring-119">[119]</a></sup> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow,_Russia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow%2C_Russia.jpg/290px-ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow%2C_Russia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow%2C_Russia.jpg/435px-ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow%2C_Russia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow%2C_Russia.jpg/580px-ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow%2C_Russia.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS-38_Nighttime_image_of_Moscow,_Russia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Moscow as viewed from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>, January 29, 2014</div></div></div></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Third_Ring_Road_(Moscow)" title="Third Ring Road (Moscow)">Third Ring Road</a>, was completed in 2003 as a high-speed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freeway" title="Freeway">freeway</a>.</li>
<li>The Fourth Transport Ring, another freeway, was planned, but cancelled in 2011. A system of chordal highways will replace it.</li></ol>
<p>Aside from the aforementioned hierarchy, line 5 of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a> is a circle-shaped <a href="/wiki/Loop_line_(railway)" title="Loop line (railway)">looped</a> subway line (hence the name <i>Koltsevaya Liniya</i>, literally "ring line"), which is located between the <i>Sadovoye Koltso</i> and Third Transport Ring.
</p><p>Two modern overlapping lines of Moscow Metro form "two hearts":
</p>
<ul><li>Line 14. Since September 10, 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Circle" title="Moscow Central Circle">Moscow Central Circle</a></i> renovated railroad (former <i>Moskovskaya Okruzhnaya Zheleznaya Doroga</i>) was introduced as Line 14 of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a>. The cone-shaped railroad initially opened in 1908 (freight-only railway from 1934 until the 2016 reopening).</li>
<li>Line 11. Another circle metro line - <i>Big Circle Line</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bolshaya_Koltsevaya_line" title="Bolshaya Koltsevaya line">Bolshaya Koltsevaya Liniya</a></i>) is under construction and will be finished in 2023. <a href="/wiki/Kakhovskaya_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Kakhovskaya (Moscow Metro)">Kakhovskaya</a>-<a href="/wiki/Savyolovskaya_(Bolshaya_Koltsevaya_line)" title="Savyolovskaya (Bolshaya Koltsevaya line)">Savyolovskaya</a> western half of the line was launched in late 2021.</li></ul>
<p>The outermost ring within Moscow is the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Ring_Road" title="Moscow Ring Road">Moscow Ring Road</a> (often called <i>MKAD</i>, acronym word for Russian <i>Московская Кольцевая Автомобильная Дорога</i>), which forms the cultural boundary of the city, was established in the 1950s. It is to note the method of building the road (usage of ground elevation instead of concrete columns throughout the whole way) formed a wall-like barrier that obstacles building roads under the MKAD highway itself).
</p>
<ul><li>Before 2012 expansion of Moscow, MKAD was considered an approximate border for Moscow boundaries.</li></ul>
<p>Outside Moscow, some of the roads encompassing the city continue to follow this circular pattern seen inside city limits, with the notable examples of <i>Betonka</i> roads (highways A107 and A108), originally made of concrete pads.
</p><p>In order to reduce transit traffic on MKAD, the new ring road (called <i>CKAD</i> - <i>Centralnaya Koltsevaya Avtomobilnaya Doroga</i>, <i>Central Ring Road</i>) is under construction now.
</p>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_at_night_(19940510886).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3680" data-file-width="5520" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Moscow_at_night_%2819940510886%29.jpg/220px-Moscow_at_night_%2819940510886%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Moscow_at_night_%2819940510886%29.jpg/330px-Moscow_at_night_%2819940510886%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Moscow_at_night_%2819940510886%29.jpg/440px-Moscow_at_night_%2819940510886%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_at_night_(19940510886).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tretyakov_Gallery" title="Tretyakov Gallery">Tretyakov Gallery</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_galleries">Museums and galleries</span></h3>
<p>One of the most notable art museums in Moscow is the <a href="/wiki/Tretyakov_Gallery" title="Tretyakov Gallery">Tretyakov Gallery</a>, which was founded by <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Tretyakov" title="Pavel Tretyakov">Pavel Tretyakov</a>, a wealthy patron of the arts who donated a large private collection to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The Tretyakov Gallery is split into two buildings. The Old Tretyakov gallery, the original gallery in the <a href="/wiki/Tretyakov_Gallery" title="Tretyakov Gallery">Tretyakovskaya</a> area on the south bank of the Moskva River, houses works in the classic Russian tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trety_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-trety-121">[121]</a></sup> The works of famous pre-<a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">Revolutionary</a> painters, such as <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Repin" title="Ilya Repin">Ilya Repin</a>, as well as the works of early Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icon_painting" title="Icon painting">icon painters</a> can be found here. Visitors can even see rare originals by early 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">iconographer</a> <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Rublev" title="Andrei Rublev">Andrei Rublev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trety_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-trety-121">[121]</a></sup>
The New Tretyakov gallery, created in Soviet times, mainly contains the works of Soviet artists, as well as of a few contemporary paintings, but there is some overlap with the Old Tretyakov Gallery for early 20th-century art. The new gallery includes a small reconstruction of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Tatlin" title="Vladimir Tatlin">Vladimir Tatlin</a>'s famous <i><a href="/wiki/Tatlin%27s_Tower" title="Tatlin's Tower">Monument to the Third International</a></i> and a mixture of other avant-garde works by artists like <a href="/wiki/Kazimir_Malevich" title="Kazimir Malevich">Kazimir Malevich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">Wassily Kandinsky</a>. Socialist realism features can also be found within the halls of the New Tretyakov Gallery.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gmii.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gmii.jpg/220px-Gmii.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gmii.jpg/330px-Gmii.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gmii.jpg/440px-Gmii.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gmii.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pushkin_Museum" title="Pushkin Museum">Pushkin Museum of Fine Arts</a></div></div></div>
<p>Another art museum in the city of Moscow is the <a href="/wiki/Pushkin_Museum" title="Pushkin Museum">Pushkin Museum of Fine Arts</a>, which was founded by, among others, the father of <a href="/wiki/Marina_Tsvetaeva" title="Marina Tsvetaeva">Marina Tsvetaeva</a>. The Pushkin Museum is similar to the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a> in London in that its halls are a cross-section of exhibits on world civilisations, with many copies of ancient sculptures. However, it also hosts paintings from every major Western era; works by <a href="/wiki/Claude_Monet" title="Claude Monet">Claude Monet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_C%C3%A9zanne" title="Paul Cézanne">Paul Cézanne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a> are present in the museum's collection.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/State_Historical_Museum" title="State Historical Museum">State Historical Museum</a> of Russia (Государственный Исторический музей) is a museum of Russian history located between Red Square and <a href="/wiki/Manezhnaya_Square,_Moscow" title="Manezhnaya Square, Moscow">Manege Square</a> in Moscow. Its exhibitions range from relics of the prehistoric tribes inhabiting present-day Russia, through priceless artworks acquired by members of the Romanov dynasty. The total number of objects in the museum's collection numbers is several million. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polytechnical_Museum" title="Polytechnical Museum">Polytechnical Museum</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> founded in 1872 is the largest technical museum in Russia, offering a wide array of historical inventions and technological achievements, including humanoid automata from the 18th century and the first Soviet computers. Its collection contains more than 160,000 items.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The Borodino Panorama<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> museum located on Kutuzov Avenue provides an opportunity for visitors to experience being on a battlefield with a 360° <a href="/wiki/Diorama" title="Diorama">diorama</a>. It is a part of the large historical memorial commemorating the victory in the Patriotic War of 1812 over Napoleon's army, that includes also the <a href="/wiki/Triumphal_Arch_of_Moscow" title="Triumphal Arch of Moscow">triumphal arch</a>, erected in 1827. There is also a military history museum that includes statues, and military hardware.
<a href="/wiki/Memorial_Museum_of_Cosmonautics" title="Memorial Museum of Cosmonautics">Memorial Museum of Cosmonautics</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Conquerors_of_Space" title="Monument to the Conquerors of Space">Monument to the Conquerors of Space</a> at the end of <a href="/wiki/Cosmonauts_Alley" title="Cosmonauts Alley">Cosmonauts Alley</a> is the central memorial place for the Russian space officials.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shchusev_State_Museum_of_Architecture" title="Shchusev State Museum of Architecture">Shchusev State Museum of Architecture</a> is the national museum of Russian architecture by the name of the architect <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Shchusev" title="Alexey Shchusev">Alexey Shchusev</a> near the Kremlin area.
</p><p>Moscow will get its own branch of the Hermitage Museum in 2024, with authorities having agreed upon the final project, to be executed by Hani Rashid, co-founder of New York-based 'Asymptote Architecture' - the same bureau that's behind the city's stock market building, the Busan-based World Business Center Solomon Tower and the Strata Tower in Abu-Dhabi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:164px;max-width:164px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:103px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%87%D1%8C%D1%8E.jpg/324px-%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%87%D1%8C%D1%8E.jpg 2x" width="162"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:103px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Inside_Moscow_Bolshoi_Theatre.jpg/222px-Inside_Moscow_Bolshoi_Theatre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Inside_Moscow_Bolshoi_Theatre.jpg/333px-Inside_Moscow_Bolshoi_Theatre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Inside_Moscow_Bolshoi_Theatre.jpg/444px-Inside_Moscow_Bolshoi_Theatre.jpg 2x" width="222"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flow-root"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">The <a href="/wiki/Bolshoi_Theatre" title="Bolshoi Theatre">Bolshoi Theatre</a></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span></h3>
<p>Moscow is the heart of the Russian performing arts, including <a href="/wiki/Russian_ballet" title="Russian ballet">ballet</a> and film, with 68 museums<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> 103<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> theaters, 132 cinemas and 24 concert halls. Among Moscow's theaters and ballet studios is the <a href="/wiki/Bolshoi_Theatre" title="Bolshoi Theatre">Bolshoi Theatre</a> and the Malyi Theatre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vakhtangov_Theatre" title="Vakhtangov Theatre">Vakhtangov Theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Art_Theatre" title="Moscow Art Theatre">Moscow Art Theatre</a>.
</p><p>The Moscow International Performance Arts Center,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> opened in 2003, also known as <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_House_of_Music" title="Moscow International House of Music">Moscow International House of Music</a>, is known for its performances in classical music. It has the largest <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)" title="Organ (music)">organ</a> in Russia installed in Svetlanov Hall.
</p><p>There are also two large circuses in Moscow: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_Circus" title="Moscow State Circus">Moscow State Circus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Circus_on_Tsvetnoy_Boulevard" title="Moscow Circus on Tsvetnoy Boulevard">Moscow Circus on Tsvetnoy Boulevard</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> named after <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Nikulin" title="Yuri Nikulin">Yuri Nikulin</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mosfilm" title="Mosfilm">Mosfilm</a> studio was at the heart of many classic films, as it is responsible for both artistic and mainstream productions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> However, despite the continued presence and reputation of internationally renowned Russian filmmakers, the once prolific native studios are much quieter. Rare and historical films may be seen in the Salut cinema, where films from the Museum of Cinema<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> collection are shown regularly. International film festivals such as the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Film_Festival" title="Moscow International Film Festival">Moscow International Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stalker_(film_festival)" title="Stalker (film festival)">Stalker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artdocfest" title="Artdocfest">Artdocfest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Jewish_Film_Festival" title="Moscow Jewish Film Festival">Moscow Jewish Film Festival</a> are staged in Moscow.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Moscow" title="Football in Moscow">Football in Moscow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LuzhnikiStadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LuzhnikiStadium.jpg/220px-LuzhnikiStadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LuzhnikiStadium.jpg/330px-LuzhnikiStadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LuzhnikiStadium.jpg/440px-LuzhnikiStadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LuzhnikiStadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2018 FIFA World Cup Final">2018 FIFA World Cup Final</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2896" data-file-width="4344" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg/220px-Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg/330px-Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg/440px-Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_05-2017_img48_Olimpiysky_Arena.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow)">SC Olimpiyskiy</a> was built for the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Over 500 Olympic sports champions lived in the city by 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Moscow is home to 63 stadiums (besides eight football and eleven light athletics maneges), of which <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a> is the largest and the 4th biggest in Europe (it hosted the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_UEFA_Cup" title="1998–99 UEFA Cup">1998–99 UEFA Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">2007–08 UEFA Champions League</a> finals, the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> with 7 games total, including the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2018 FIFA World Cup Final">final</a>). Forty other sports complexes are located within the city, including 24 with artificial ice. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow_arena)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow arena)">Olympic Stadium</a> was the world's first indoor arena for <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a> and hosted the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship" title="Bandy World Championship">Bandy World Championship</a> twice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Moscow was again the host of the competition in 2010, this time in <a href="/wiki/Ice_Palace_Krylatskoye" title="Ice Palace Krylatskoye">Krylatskoye</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> That arena has also hosted the <a href="/wiki/World_Speed_Skating_Championships" title="World Speed Skating Championships">World Speed Skating Championships</a>. There are also seven <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a> tracks in Moscow,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-109">[109]</a></sup> of which <a href="/wiki/Central_Moscow_Hippodrome" title="Central Moscow Hippodrome">Central Moscow Hippodrome</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> founded in 1834, is the largest.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CSKA_Arena_(Quintin_Soloviev).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/CSKA_Arena_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/220px-CSKA_Arena_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/CSKA_Arena_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/330px-CSKA_Arena_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/CSKA_Arena_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/440px-CSKA_Arena_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CSKA_Arena_(Quintin_Soloviev).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CSKA_Arena" title="CSKA Arena">CSKA Arena</a> during a game of <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">KHL</a>, considered to be the second-best ice hockey league in the world</div></div></div>
<p>Moscow was the host city of the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Yachting" title="Yachting">yachting</a> events being held at <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>. Large sports facilities and the main international airport, Sheremetyevo Terminal 2, were built in preparation for the 1980 Summer Olympics. Moscow had made a bid for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. However, when final voting commenced on July 6, 2005, Moscow was the first city to be eliminated from further rounds. The Games were awarded to <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">London</a>.
</p><p>The most titled <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team in the Soviet Union and in the world, <a href="/wiki/HC_CSKA_Moscow" title="HC CSKA Moscow">HC CSKA Moscow</a> comes from Moscow. Other big ice hockey clubs from Moscow are <a href="/wiki/HC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="HC Dynamo Moscow">HC Dynamo Moscow</a>, which was the second most titled team in the Soviet Union, and <a href="/wiki/HC_Spartak_Moscow" title="HC Spartak Moscow">HC Spartak Moscow</a>.
</p><p>The most titled Soviet, Russian, and one of the most titled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euroleague" title="Euroleague">Euroleague</a> clubs, is the <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> club from Moscow <a href="/wiki/PBC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PBC CSKA Moscow">PBC CSKA Moscow</a>. Moscow hosted the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">EuroBasket</a> in 1953 and 1965.
</p><p>Moscow had more winners at the <a href="/wiki/USSR_Chess_Championship" title="USSR Chess Championship">USSR</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Chess_Championship" title="Russian Chess Championship">Russian Chess Championship</a> than any other city.
</p><p>The most titled <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> team in the Soviet Union and in Europe (<a href="/wiki/CEV_Champions_League" title="CEV Champions League">CEV Champions League</a>) is <a href="/wiki/VC_CSKA_Moscow" title="VC CSKA Moscow">VC CSKA Moscow</a>.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak_Moscow" title="FC Spartak Moscow">FC Spartak Moscow</a> has won more championship titles in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Premier_League" title="Russian Premier League">Russian Premier League</a> than any other team. They were second only to <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">FC Dynamo Kyiv</a> in <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">Soviet times</a>. <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">PFC CSKA Moscow</a> became the first Russian football team to win a <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> title, the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_UEFA_Cup" title="2004–05 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>). <a href="/wiki/FC_Lokomotiv_Moscow" title="FC Lokomotiv Moscow">FC Lokomotiv Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Moscow" title="FC Dynamo Moscow">FC Dynamo Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Torpedo_Moscow" title="FC Torpedo Moscow">FC Torpedo Moscow</a> are other professional football teams also based in Moscow.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 265px"><div style="width: 265px">

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 265px"><div style="width: 265px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 260px;"><div style="margin:37.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg" title="RZD Arena, home of FC Lokomotiv Moscow"><img alt="RZD Arena, home of FC Lokomotiv Moscow" data-file-height="501" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg/230px-Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg/345px-Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg/460px-Lokomotiv_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RZD_Arena" title="RZD Arena">RZD Arena</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/FC_Lokomotiv_Moscow" title="FC Lokomotiv Moscow">FC Lokomotiv Moscow</a>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Moscow houses other prominent football, ice hockey, and basketball teams. Because sports organisations in the Soviet Union were once highly centralized, two of the best Union-level teams represented defence and law-enforcing agencies: the Armed Forces (<a href="/wiki/CSKA_Moscow" title="CSKA Moscow">CSKA</a>) and the Ministry of Internal Affairs (<a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Sports_Club" title="Dynamo Sports Club">Dinamo</a>). There were army and police teams in most major cities. As a result, Spartak, CSKA, and Dinamo were among the best-funded teams in the USSR.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Irina_Viner-Usmanova_Gymnastics_Palace" title="Irina Viner-Usmanova Gymnastics Palace">Irina Viner-Usmanova Gymnastics Palace</a> is located in the <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Olympic_Complex" title="Luzhniki Olympic Complex">Luzniki Olympic Complex</a>. The building works started in 2017 and the opening ceremony took place on June 18, 2019. The investor of the Palace is the billionaire <a href="/wiki/Alisher_Usmanov" title="Alisher Usmanov">Alisher Usmanov</a>, husband of the former gymnast and gymnastics coach <a href="/wiki/Irina_Viner-Usmanova" title="Irina Viner-Usmanova">Irina Viner-Usmanova</a>. The total surface of the building is 23,500 m<sup>2</sup>, which include 3 fitness rooms, locker rooms, rooms reserved for referees and coaches, saunas, a canteen, a cafeteria, 2 ball halls, a Medical center, a hall reserved for journalists, and a hotel for athletes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because of Moscow's cold local climate, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">winter sports</a> have a following. Many of Moscow's large parks offer marked trails for skiing and frozen ponds for skating.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg/220px-2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg/330px-2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg/440px-2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2018_World_Cup_Final_-_France_v_Croatia_-_1st_Half.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a> in Moscow, which hosted games of the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Moscow hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Kremlin_Cup" title="Kremlin Cup">Kremlin Cup</a>, a popular tennis tournament on both the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">WTA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">ATP</a> tours. It is one of the ten Tier-I events on the women's tour and a host of Russian players feature every year.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow)">SC Olimpiyskiy</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2009" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2009">Eurovision Song Contest 2009</a>, the first and so far the only <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> arranged in Russia.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Slava_Moscow" title="Slava Moscow">Slava Moscow</a> is a professional <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> club, competing in the national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_Rugby_League" title="Professional Rugby League">Professional Rugby League</a>. Former <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> heavyweights <a href="/wiki/RC_Lokomotiv_Moscow" title="RC Lokomotiv Moscow">RC Lokomotiv</a> have entered the same league as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. The Luzhniki Stadium also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_World_Cup_Sevens" title="2013 Rugby World Cup Sevens">2013 Rugby World Cup Sevens</a>.
</p><p>In bandy, one of the most successful clubs in the world is 20 times <a href="/wiki/Russian_Bandy_Super_League" title="Russian Bandy Super League">Russian League</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Moscow_Bandy_Club" title="Dynamo Moscow Bandy Club">Dynamo Moscow</a>. They have also won the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Cup" title="Bandy World Cup">World Cup</a> thrice and <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_(bandy)" title="European Cup (bandy)">European Cup</a> six times.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/MFK_Dinamo_Moskva" title="MFK Dinamo Moskva">MFK Dinamo Moskva</a> is one of the major <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> clubs in Europe, having won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Futsal_Champions_League" title="UEFA Futsal Champions League">Futsal Champions League</a> title once.
</p><p>When Russia was selected to host the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, the Luzhniki Stadium got an increased capacity, by almost 10,000 new seats, in addition to a further two stadiums that have been built: the <a href="/wiki/VTB_Arena" title="VTB Arena">Dynamo Stadium</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otkrytiye_Arena" title="Otkrytiye Arena">Spartak Stadium</a>, although the first one later was dismissed from having World Cup matches.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Moscow" title="List of shopping malls in Moscow">List of shopping malls in Moscow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2667" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg/220px-Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg/330px-Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg/440px-Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arbat_Street_in_MSK.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Arbat_Street" title="Arbat Street">Arbat Street</a>, in the historical centre of Moscow</div></div></div>
<p>The city is full of clubs, restaurants, and bars. <a href="/wiki/Tverskaya_Street" title="Tverskaya Street">Tverskaya Street</a> is also one of the busiest shopping streets in Moscow.
</p><p>The adjoining <a href="/wiki/Tretyakovsky_Proyezd" title="Tretyakovsky Proyezd">Tretyakovsky Proyezd</a>, also south of Tverskaya Street, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitai-gorod" title="Kitai-gorod">Kitai-gorod</a>, is host to upmarket boutique stores such as <a href="/wiki/Bulgari" title="Bulgari">Bulgari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bentley" title="Bentley">Bentley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go-mag_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-go-mag-138">[138]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">Nightlife</a> in Moscow has moved on since Soviet times and today the city has many of the world's largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nightclubs" title="Nightclubs">nightclubs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Clubs, bars, creative spaces and restaurants-turned-into-dancefloors are flooding Moscow streets with new openings every year. The hottest area is located around the old chocolate factory, where bars, nightclubs, galleries, cafés and restaurants are placed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dream_Island_(amusement_park)" title="Dream Island (amusement park)">Dream Island</a> is an amusement park in Moscow that opened on February 29, 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> It is the largest indoor theme park in Europe.
The park covers 300,000 square meters. During the park's construction, 150 acres of nature trees unique and rare animals and birds and plants on the peninsula were destroyed. The appearance is in the style of a fairytale castle similar to Disneyland. The park has 29 unique attractions with many rides, as well as pedestrian malls with fountains and cycle paths. The complex includes a landscaped park along with a concert hall, a cinema, a hotel, a children's sailing school, restaurants, and shops.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Authorities">Authorities</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_authorities">Moscow authorities</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Moscow" title="Government of Moscow">Government of Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Moscow" title="Mayor of Moscow">Mayor of Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moscow_City_Duma" title="Moscow City Duma">Moscow City Duma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_city_of_Moscow" title="Charter of the city of Moscow">Charter of the city of Moscow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2734" data-file-width="3417" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg/220px-Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg/330px-Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg/440px-Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Government_of_Moscow" title="Government of Moscow">Government of Moscow</a></div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of the Russian Federation</a>, Moscow is an independent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_subject" title="Federal subject">federal subject</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian Federation</a>, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">city of federal importance</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Moscow" title="Mayor of Moscow">Mayor of Moscow</a> is the leading official in the executive, leading the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Moscow" title="Government of Moscow">Government of Moscow</a>, which is the highest organ of executive power.
The Moscow City Duma is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_Duma" title="City Duma">City Duma</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a> or local <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>) and local laws must be approved by it. It includes 45 members who are elected for a five-year term on <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">Single-mandate constituency</a> basis.
</p><p>From 2006 to 2012, direct elections of the mayor were not held due to changes in the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_city_of_Moscow" title="Charter of the city of Moscow">Charter of the city of Moscow</a>, the mayor was appointed by presidential decree. The first direct elections from the time of the <a href="/wiki/2003_Moscow_mayoral_election" title="2003 Moscow mayoral election">2003 vote</a> were to be held after the expiration of the current mayor in 2015, however, in connection with his resignation of his own free will, they took place in <a href="/wiki/2013_Moscow_mayoral_election" title="2013 Moscow mayoral election">September 2013</a>.
</p><p>Local administration is carried out through eleven prefectures, uniting the districts of Moscow into administrative districts on a territorial basis, and 125 regional administrations. According to the law "On the organization of local self-government in the city of Moscow", since the beginning of 2003, the executive bodies of local self-government are municipalities, representative bodies are municipal assemblies, whose members are elected in accordance with the Charter of the intracity municipality.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_authorities">Federal authorities</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/White_House_(Moscow)" title="White House (Moscow)">White House (Moscow)</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg/220px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg/330px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg/440px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%A0%D0%A4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/White_House_(Moscow)" title="White House (Moscow)">The House of the Government of the Russian Federation</a></div></div></div>
<p>In Moscow, as in a city endowed with the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of the Russian Federation</a>, the legislative, executive, and judicial federal authorities of the country are located, with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Russia" title="Constitutional Court of Russia">Constitutional Court of the Russian Federation</a>, which has been located in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> since 2008.
</p><p>The supreme executive authority - the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Government of the Russian Federation</a> - is located in the <a href="/wiki/White_House_(Moscow)" title="White House (Moscow)">House of the Government of the Russian Federation</a> on <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F" title="ru:Краснопресненская набережная">Krasnopresnenskaya embankment</a> in the center of Moscow. The <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a> sits on <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9E%D1%85%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%A0%D1%8F%D0%B4" title="ru:Охотный Ряд">Okhotny Ryad</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Federation_Council_(Russia)" title="Federation Council (Russia)">Federation Council</a> is located in a building on <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%94%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BA%D0%B0" title="ru:Улица Большая Дмитровка">Bolshaya Dmitrovka</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Russia" title="Supreme Court of Russia">Supreme Court of the Russian Federation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Arbitration_of_Russia" title="Supreme Court of Arbitration of Russia">Supreme Court of Arbitration of the Russian Federation</a> are also located in Moscow.
</p><p>In addition, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">Moscow Kremlin</a> is the official residence of the President of the Russian Federation. The president's working residence in the Kremlin is located in the <a href="/wiki/Kremlin_Senate" title="Kremlin Senate">Senate Palace</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Police_bmw.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Police_bmw.jpg/220px-Police_bmw.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Police_bmw.jpg/330px-Police_bmw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Police_bmw.jpg/440px-Police_bmw.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Police_bmw.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/BMW_5_Series" title="BMW 5 Series">BMW 5 Series</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_City_Police" title="Moscow City Police">Moscow Police</a> on patrol</div></div></div>
<p>According to the ranking of the safest cities made by <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">The Economist</a> Moscow occupies the 37th position with a score of 68,5 points percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The general level of crime is quite low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> More than 170,000 surveillance cameras in Moscow are connected to the facial recognition system. The authorities recognized the successful two-month experiment with automatic recognition of faces, gender, and age of people in real-time - and then they deployed the system to the whole city. The network of video surveillance unites access video cameras (95% of residential apartment buildings in the capital), cameras in the territory and in buildings of schools and kindergartens, at the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Circle" title="Moscow Central Circle">MCC</a> stations, stadiums, public transport stops, and bus stations, in parks, underground passages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>The emergency numbers are the same as in all the other regions of Russia: 112 is the Single Emergency Number, 101 is the number of the Fire Service and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Emergency_Situations_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Emergency Situations (Russia)">Ministry of Emergency Situations</a>, 102 is the <a href="/wiki/Police_of_Russia" title="Police of Russia">Police</a> one, 103 is the ambulance one, 104 is the Emergency Gas number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Moscow's EMS is the second most efficient one among the world's megacities, as reported by PwC during the presentation of the international study Analysis of EMS Efficiency in Megacities of the World.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The entire city of Moscow is headed by one mayor (<a href="/wiki/Sergey_Sobyanin" title="Sergey Sobyanin">Sergey Sobyanin</a>). The city of Moscow is divided into twelve administrative okrugs and 125 districts.
</p><p>The Russian capital's town-planning development began to show as early as the 12th century when the city was founded. The central part of Moscow grew by consolidating with suburbs in line with medieval principles of urban development when strong fortress walls would gradually spread along the circle streets of adjacent new settlements. The first circular defence walls set the trajectory of Moscow's rings, laying the groundwork for the future planning of the Russian capital.
</p><p>The following fortifications served as the city's circular defense boundaries at some point in history: the Kremlin walls, Zemlyanoy Gorod (Earthwork Town), the Kamer-Kollezhsky Rampart, the Garden Ring, and the small railway ring. The Moscow Ring Road (MKAD) has been Moscow's boundary since 1960. Also in the form of a circle are the main Moscow subway line, the Ring Line, and the so-called Third Automobile Ring, which was completed in 2005. Hence, the characteristic radial-circle planning continues to define Moscow's further development. However, contemporary Moscow has also engulfed a number of territories outside the MKAD, such as Solntsevo, Butovo, and the town of <a href="/wiki/Zelenograd" title="Zelenograd">Zelenograd</a>. A part of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a>'s territory was merged into Moscow on July 1, 2012; as a result, Moscow is no longer fully surrounded by Moscow Oblast and now also has a border with <a href="/wiki/Kaluga_Oblast" title="Kaluga Oblast">Kaluga Oblast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merger_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merger-148">[148]</a></sup> In all, Moscow gained about 1,500 square kilometers (580 sq mi) and 230,000 inhabitants. Moscow's Mayor Sergey Sobyanin lauded the expansion that will help Moscow and the neighboring region, a "mega-city" of twenty million people, to develop "harmonically."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merger2_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Merger2-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>All administrative okrugs and districts have their own <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coats of arms</a> and flags as well as individual heads of the area.
</p><p>In addition to the districts, there are Territorial Units with Special Status. These usually include areas with small or no permanent populations. Such is the case with the All-Russia Exhibition Centre, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Botanical_Garden_of_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Moscow Botanical Garden of Academy of Sciences">Botanical Garden</a>, large parks, and industrial zones. In recent years, some territories have been merged with different districts. There are no ethnic-specific regions in Moscow, as in the <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatowns</a> that exist in some <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asian</a> cities. And although districts are not designated by income, as with most cities, those areas that are closer to the city center, metro stations or green zones are considered more prestigious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>Moscow also hosts some of the government bodies of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a>, although the city itself is not a part of the oblast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoscowO_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-MoscowO-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
