<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg/220px-Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg/330px-Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg/440px-Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">Moscow International Business Center</a>, one of the largest financial centres of Europe and the world</div></div></div>
<p>Moscow has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">largest municipal economies in Europe</a> and it accounts more than one-fifth of Russia's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_Regional_Product" title="Gross Regional Product">GRP</a> of Moscow reached almost ₽20 trillion(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>330 billion)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> and ₽1,567,645 per capita(~US$26,000). Gross Metropolitan Product(Moscow + Moscow Region) was over ₽25 trillion or around US$420 billion.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1333" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg/170px-Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg/255px-Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg/340px-Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Exhacnge_main_building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moscow_Exchange" title="Moscow Exchange">Moscow Exchange</a></div></div></div>
<p>Moscow has the lowest unemployment rate of all <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a>, standing at just 1% in 2010, compared to the national average of 7%. The average gross monthly wage in the city is ₽60,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>2,500 in Purchasing Power<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-155">[155]</a></sup>), which is almost twice the national average of ₽34,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>1,400 in Purchasing Power<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-155">[155]</a></sup>), and the highest among the federal subjects of Russia.
</p><p>Moscow is home to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_number_of_billionaires" title="List of cities by number of billionaires">third-highest number of billionaires</a> of any city in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> and has the highest number of billionaires of any city in Europe. It is the financial center of Russia and home to the country's largest banks and many of its largest companies, such as oil giant <a href="/wiki/Rosneft" title="Rosneft">Rosneft</a>. Moscow accounts for 17% of retail sales in Russia and for 13% of all construction activity in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bofit_42_2010_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-bofit_42_2010-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis" title="1998 Russian financial crisis">1998 Russian financial crisis</a>, business sectors in Moscow have shown exponential rates of growth. Many new business centers and office buildings have been built in recent years, but Moscow still experiences shortages in office space. As a result, many former industrial and research facilities are being reconstructed to become suitable for office use. Overall, economic stability has improved in recent years; nonetheless, crime and corruption still hinder business development.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h3>
<p>Primary <a href="/wiki/Industry_(economics)" title="Industry (economics)">industries</a> in Moscow include the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_production" title="Energy production">energy production</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machine" title="Machine">machinery</a> industries.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mil_Moscow_Helicopter_Plant" title="Mil Moscow Helicopter Plant">Mil Moscow Helicopter Plant</a> is one of the world's leading producers of military and civil helicopters. <a href="/wiki/Khrunichev_State_Research_and_Production_Space_Center" title="Khrunichev State Research and Production Space Center">Khrunichev State Research and Production Space Center</a> produces various space equipment, including modules for space stations <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salyut" title="Salyut">Salyut</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton_(rocket)" title="Proton (rocket)">Proton launch vehicles</a> and military <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICBM" title="ICBM">ICBMs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi" title="Sukhoi">Sukhoi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin" title="Ilyushin">Ilyushin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan" title="Mikoyan">Mikoyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tupolev" title="Tupolev">Tupolev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev" title="Yakovlev">Yakovlev</a> aircraft design bureaus also situated in Moscow. <a href="/wiki/NPO_Energomash" title="NPO Energomash">NPO Energomash</a>, producing the <a href="/wiki/Rocket_engine" title="Rocket engine">rocket engines</a> for Russian and American space programs, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lavochkin" title="Lavochkin">Lavochkin</a> design bureau, which built <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fighter_plane" title="Fighter plane">fighter planes</a> during WWII, but switched to <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probes</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>, are in nearby <a href="/wiki/Khimki" title="Khimki">Khimki</a>, an independent city in <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a> that have largely been enclosed by Moscow from its sides. Automobile plants <a href="/wiki/ZiL" title="ZiL">ZiL</a> and <a href="/wiki/AZLK" title="AZLK">AZLK</a>, as well as the Voitovich Rail Vehicle plant, are situated in Moscow and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metrovagonmash" title="Metrovagonmash">Metrovagonmash</a> metro wagon plant is located just outside the city limits. The <a href="/wiki/Poljot" title="Poljot">Poljot Moscow watch factory</a> produces military, professional and sport watches well known in Russia and abroad. <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> in his trip into space used "Shturmanskie" produced by this factory.
</p><p>The Electrozavod factory was the first transformer factory in Russia. The Kristall distillery<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> is the oldest distillery in Russia producing <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a> types, including "<a href="/wiki/Stolichnaya" title="Stolichnaya">Stolichnaya</a>" while wines are produced at Moscow wine plants, including the Moscow Interrepublican Vinery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The Moscow Jewelry Factory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> and the Jewellerprom<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> are producers of jewelry in Russia; Jewellerprom used to produce the exclusive <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Victory" title="Order of Victory">Order of Victory</a>, awarded to those aiding the Soviet Union's Red Army during World War II.
</p><p>There are other industries located just outside the city of Moscow, as well as microelectronic industries in Zelenograd, including <a href="/wiki/Ruselectronics" title="Ruselectronics">Ruselectronics</a> companies.
</p><p>Gazprom, the largest extractor of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> in the world and the largest <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Russia" title="Economy of Russia">Russian company</a>, has head offices also in Moscow, as well as other oil, gas, and electricity companies.
</p><p>Moscow hosts headquarters of the many of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunication</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology</a> companies, including <a href="/wiki/1C_Company" title="1C Company">1C</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABBYY" title="ABBYY">ABBYY</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beeline_(brand)" title="Beeline (brand)">Beeline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaspersky_Lab" title="Kaspersky Lab">Kaspersky Lab</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mail.Ru" title="Mail.Ru">Mail.Ru Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/MegaFon" title="MegaFon">MegaFon</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTS_(network_provider)" title="MTS (network provider)">MTS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rambler_(portal)" title="Rambler (portal)">Rambler&amp;Co</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rostelecom" title="Rostelecom">Rostelecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yandex" title="Yandex">Yandex</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yota" title="Yota">Yota</a>.
</p><p>Some industry is being transferred out of the city to improve the ecological state of the city.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_of_living">Cost of living</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hotels_in_Moscow" title="Hotels in Moscow">Hotels in Moscow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3876" data-file-width="2584" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg/170px-Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg/255px-Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg/340px-Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_09-13_img11_Tretyakovsky_Passage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tretyakovsky_Proyezd" title="Tretyakovsky Proyezd">Tretyakovsky Proyezd</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2531" data-file-width="3811" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg/220px-2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg/330px-2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg/440px-2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2019-07-25-3032-Moscow-Nikolskaya-Street.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nikolskaya_Street" title="Nikolskaya Street">Nikolskaya Street</a></div></div></div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> times, apartments were lent to people by the government according to the square meters-per-person norm (some groups, including people's artists, heroes, and prominent scientists had bonuses according to their honors). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_ownership" title="Private ownership">Private ownership</a> of apartments was limited until the 1990s when people were permitted to secure property rights to their inhabited places. Since the Soviet era, estate owners have had to pay the service charge for their residences, a fixed amount based on persons per living area.
</p><p>The price of <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a> in Moscow continues to rise. Today, one could expect to pay $4,000 on average per square meter (11 sq ft) on the outskirts of the city<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> or US$6,500–$8,000 per square meter in a prestigious district. The price sometimes may exceed US$40,000 per square meter in a flat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> It costs about US$1,200 per month to rent a one-bedroom apartment and about US$1,000 per month for a studio in the center of Moscow.
</p><p>A typical one-bedroom apartment is about thirty square metres (320 <a href="/wiki/Square_foot" title="Square foot">square feet</a>), a typical two-bedroom apartment is forty-five square metres (480 square feet), and a typical three-bedroom apartment is seventy square metres (750 square feet). Many cannot move out of their apartments, especially if a family lives in a two-room apartment originally granted by the state during the Soviet era. Some city residents have attempted to cope with the cost of living by renting their apartments while staying in <a href="/wiki/Dacha" title="Dacha">dachas</a> (country houses) outside the city.
</p><p>In 2006, Mercer Human Resources Consulting named Moscow the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">most expensive city for expatriate employees</a>, ahead of perennial winner Tokyo, due to the stable <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> as well as increasing housing prices within the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Moscow also ranked first in the 2007 edition and 2008 edition of the survey. However, Tokyo has overtaken Moscow as the most expensive city in the world, placing Moscow at third behind Osaka in second place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mercer.com_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-mercer.com-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Moscow ranked top on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities" title="List of most expensive cities">list of most expensive cities</a> for the third year in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, according to <i>Forbes</i>, Moscow was ranked the 9th most expensive city in the world. <i>Forbes</i> ranked Moscow the 2nd most expensive city the year prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019 the Economist Intelligence Unit's Worldwide Cost of Living survey put Moscow to 102nd place in the biannual ranking of 133 most expensive cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> ECA International's Cost of Living 2019 Survey ranked Moscow at number 120 among 482 locations worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_utilities">Public utilities</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Heating">Heating</span></h4>
<p>The heating of buildings in Moscow, like in other cities in Russia is done using <a href="/wiki/District_heating" title="District heating">central heating system</a>. Before 2004, state <a href="/wiki/Unitary_enterprise" title="Unitary enterprise">unitary enterprises</a> were responsible to produce and supply heat to the clients by the operation of heating stations and heating distribution system of Mosgorteplo, Mosteploenergo, and Teploremontnaladka which gave service to the <a href="/wiki/District_heating_substation" title="District heating substation">heating substations</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Moscow" title="Administrative divisions of Moscow">north-eastern part</a> of the city. Clients were divided between the various enterprises based on their geographical location. A major reform launched in 2004 consolidated the various companies under the umbrella of MIPC which became the municipal heat supplier. Its subsidiaries were the newly transformed Joint-stock companies. The city's main source of heating is the power station of Mosenergo which was reformed in 2005, when around ten subsidiaries were separated from it. One of the newly independent companies was the District Heating Network Company (MTK) (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Московская теплосетевая компания</span>). In 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Moscow" title="Government of Moscow">Government of Moscow</a> bought controlling stakes in the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="City_services">City services</span></h4>
<p>“Our city” is a geo-information portal created in 2011 under the mayor of Moscow Sergei Sobyanin with the aim of building a constructive dialogue between Moscow residents and the city's executive authorities. The portal is being developed by the State Public Institution “New Management Technologies” together with the Moscow Department of Information Technologies. In its 10 years of operation, more than 1.7 million users have joined the portal, and during this time it has become an effective tool for monitoring the state of urban infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Russia" title="Education in Russia">Education in Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3,_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2610" data-file-width="3946" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3,_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are 1,696 high schools in Moscow, as well as 91 colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-109">[109]</a></sup> Besides these, there are 222 institutions of higher education, including 60 state universities<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_109-3"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-109">[109]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Lomonosov Moscow State University</a>, which was founded in 1755.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msu-history_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-msu-history-176">[176]</a></sup> The main university building located in Vorobyovy Gory (<a href="/wiki/Sparrow_Hills" title="Sparrow Hills">Sparrow Hills</a>) is 240 metres (790 ft) tall and when completed, was the tallest building on the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The university has over 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> and 7,000 <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">postgraduate</a> students, who have a choice of twenty-nine faculties and 450 departments for study. Additionally, approximately 10,000 high school students take courses at the university, while over two thousand researchers work. The Moscow State University library contains over nine million books, making it one of the largest libraries in all of Russia. Its acclaim throughout the international academic community has meant that over 11,000 international students have graduated from the university, with many coming to Moscow to become fluent in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I.M._Sechenov_First_Moscow_State_Medical_University" title="I.M. Sechenov First Moscow State Medical University">I.M. Sechenov First Moscow State Medical University</a> named after <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sechenov" title="Ivan Sechenov">Ivan Sechenov</a> or formerly known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Medical_Academy" title="Moscow Medical Academy">Moscow Medical Academy</a> (1stMSMU) is a medical university situated in Moscow, Russia. It was founded in 1785 as the faculty of the Moscow State University. It is a Russian Federal Agency for Health and Social Development. It is one of the largest medical universities in Russia and Europe. More than 9200 students are enrolled in 115 academic departments. It offers courses for post-graduate studies.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1154" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg/220px-Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg/330px-Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg/440px-Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University_Frontal_View.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University" title="Pirogov Russian National Research Medical University">Pirogov Russian National Research Medical University</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirogov_Russian_National_Research_Medical_University" title="Pirogov Russian National Research Medical University">Pirogov Russian National Research Medical University</a> (formerly known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_State_Medical_University" title="Russian State Medical University">Russian State Medical University</a>) is a medical higher education institution in Moscow, Russia founded in 1906. It is fully accredited and recognized by Russia's Ministry of Education and Science and is currently under the authority of the Ministry of Health and Social Development. Named after Russian surgeon and pedagogue <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Pirogov" title="Nikolay Pirogov">N.I. Pirogov</a> (1810-1888), it is one of the largest medical institutions and the first university in Russia to allow women to acquire degrees.
</p><p>Moscow is one of the financial centers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> countries and is known for its business schools. Among them are the <a href="/wiki/Financial_University_under_the_Government_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Financial University under the Government of the Russian Federation">Financial University under the Government of the Russian Federation</a>; <a href="/wiki/Plekhanov_Russian_University_of_Economics" title="Plekhanov Russian University of Economics">Plekhanov Russian University of Economics</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_State_University_of_Management" title="The State University of Management">The State University of Management</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Research_University_-_Higher_School_of_Economics" title="National Research University - Higher School of Economics">National Research University - Higher School of Economics</a>. They offer undergraduate degrees in management, finance, accounting, marketing, real estate, and economic theory, as well as Masters programs and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MBA" title="MBA">MBAs</a>. Most of them have branches in other regions of Russia and countries around the world.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4159" data-file-width="7394" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg/220px-Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg/330px-Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg/440px-Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_MSTU_Bauman_main_building_asv2021-08.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main building of the <a href="/wiki/Bauman_Moscow_State_Technical_University" title="Bauman Moscow State Technical University">Bauman Moscow State Technical University</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bauman_Moscow_State_Technical_University" title="Bauman Moscow State Technical University">Bauman Moscow State Technical University</a>, founded in 1830, is located in the center of Moscow and provides 18,000 undergraduate and 1,000 postgraduate students with an education in science and engineering, offering technical degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2875" data-file-width="4312" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg/220px-Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg/330px-Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg/440px-Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_05-2017_img41_Conservatory.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conservatory" title="Moscow Conservatory">Moscow Conservatory</a> building</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conservatory" title="Moscow Conservatory">Moscow Conservatory</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> founded in 1866, is a prominent music school in Russia whose graduates include <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Rachmaninoff" title="Sergei Rachmaninoff">Sergey Rachmaninoff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Scriabin" title="Alexander Scriabin">Alexander Scriabin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aram_Khachaturian" title="Aram Khachaturian">Aram Khachaturian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_Rostropovich" title="Mstislav Rostropovich">Mstislav Rostropovich</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Schnittke" title="Alfred Schnittke">Alfred Schnittke</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vgik.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2188" data-file-width="2856" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vgik.jpg/220px-Vgik.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vgik.jpg/330px-Vgik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vgik.jpg/440px-Vgik.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vgik.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Gerasimov_Institute_of_Cinematography" title="Gerasimov Institute of Cinematography">Russian State Institute of Cinematography</a>, the world's oldest<br/><a href="/wiki/Film_school" title="Film school">film school</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gerasimov_Institute_of_Cinematography" title="Gerasimov Institute of Cinematography">Gerasimov All-Russian State Institute of Cinematography</a>, abbreviated as VGIK, is the world's oldest educational institution in <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">Cinematography</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Gardin" title="Vladimir Gardin">Vladimir Gardin</a> in 1919.
<a href="/wiki/Sergei_Eisenstein" title="Sergei Eisenstein">Sergei Eisenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vsevolod_Pudovkin" title="Vsevolod Pudovkin">Vsevolod Pudovkin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aleksey_Batalov" title="Aleksey Batalov">Aleksey Batalov</a> were among its most distinguished professors and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Vartanov" title="Mikhail Vartanov">Mikhail Vartanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Parajanov" title="Sergei Parajanov">Sergei Parajanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Tarkovsky" title="Andrei Tarkovsky">Andrei Tarkovsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Mikhalkov" title="Nikita Mikhalkov">Nikita Mikhalkov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eldar_Ryazanov" title="Eldar Ryazanov">Eldar Ryazanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Sokurov" title="Alexander Sokurov">Alexander Sokurov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuriy_Norshteyn" title="Yuriy Norshteyn">Yuriy Norshteyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Petrov_(animator)" title="Aleksandr Petrov (animator)">Aleksandr Petrov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Shukshin" title="Vasily Shukshin">Vasily Shukshin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Wolf" title="Konrad Wolf">Konrad Wolf</a> among graduates.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_Institute_of_International_Relations" title="Moscow State Institute of International Relations">Moscow State Institute of International Relations</a>, founded in 1944, remains Russia's best- known school of international relations and diplomacy, with six schools focused on international relations. Approximately 4,500 students make up the university's student body and over 700,000 Russian and foreign-language books—of which 20,000 are considered rare—can be found in the library of the Moscow State Institute of International Relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other institutions are the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Institute_of_Physics_and_Technology" title="Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology">Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology</a>, also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phystech" title="Phystech">Phystech</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fyodorov_Eye_Microsurgery_Complex" title="Fyodorov Eye Microsurgery Complex">Fyodorov Eye Microsurgery Complex</a>, founded in 1988 by Russian eye surgeon <a href="/wiki/Svyatoslav_Fyodorov" title="Svyatoslav Fyodorov">Svyatoslav Fyodorov</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Aviation_Institute" title="Moscow Aviation Institute">Moscow Aviation Institute</a>, the Moscow Motorway Institute (State Technical University), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Engineering_Physics_Institute" title="Moscow Engineering Physics Institute">Moscow Engineering Physics Institute</a>. <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Institute_of_Physics_and_Technology" title="Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology">Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology</a> has taught numerous <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners, including <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Kapitsa" title="Pyotr Kapitsa">Pyotr Kapitsa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Semyonov" title="Nikolay Semyonov">Nikolay Semyonov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lev_Landau" title="Lev Landau">Lev Landau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Prokhorov" title="Alexander Prokhorov">Alexander Prokhorov</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Engineering_Physics_Institute" title="Moscow Engineering Physics Institute">Moscow Engineering Physics Institute</a> is known for its research in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The highest Russian military school is the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Arms_Academy_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Combined Arms Academy of the Armed Forces of the Russian Federation">Combined Arms Academy of the Armed Forces of the Russian Federation</a>.
</p><p>Although Moscow has a number of famous Soviet-era higher educational institutions, most of which are more oriented towards engineering or the fundamental sciences, in recent years Moscow has seen a growth in the number of commercial and private institutions that offer classes in business and management. Many state institutions have expanded their education scope and introduced new courses or departments. Institutions in Moscow, as well as the rest of post-Soviet Russia, have begun to offer new international certificates and postgraduate degrees, including the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Business_Administration" title="Master of Business Administration">Master of Business Administration</a>. <a href="/wiki/Student_exchange_program" title="Student exchange program">Student exchange programs</a> with numerous countries, specially with the rest of Europe, have also become widespread in Moscow's universities, while schools within the Russian capital also offer seminars, lectures, and courses for corporate employees and businessmen.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_1152_(14384525084).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5380" data-file-width="3587" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Moscow_1152_%2814384525084%29.jpg/170px-Moscow_1152_%2814384525084%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Moscow_1152_%2814384525084%29.jpg/255px-Moscow_1152_%2814384525084%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Moscow_1152_%2814384525084%29.jpg/340px-Moscow_1152_%2814384525084%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_1152_(14384525084).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a></div></div></div>
<p>Moscow is one of the largest science centers in Russia. The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> are located in Moscow as well as research and applied science institutions. The <a href="/wiki/Kurchatov_Institute" title="Kurchatov Institute">Kurchatov Institute</a>, Russia's leading research and development institution in the fields of nuclear energy, where the first <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> in Europe was built, the <a href="/wiki/Landau_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics" title="Landau Institute for Theoretical Physics">Landau Institute for Theoretical Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Theoretical_and_Experimental_Physics" title="Institute for Theoretical and Experimental Physics">Institute for Theoretical and Experimental Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Physical_Problems" title="Institute for Physical Problems">Kapitza Institute for Physical Problems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steklov_Institute_of_Mathematics" title="Steklov Institute of Mathematics">Steklov Institute of Mathematics</a> are all situated in Moscow.
</p><p>There are 452 libraries in the city, including 168 for children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_109-4"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-109">[109]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Russian_State_Library" title="Russian State Library">Russian State Library</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> founded in 1862, is the national library of Russia. The library is home to over 275 km (171 mi) of shelves and 42 million items, including over 17 million books and serial volumes, 13 million journals, 350,000 music scores and sound records, and 150,000 maps, making it the largest library in Russia and one of the largest in the world. Items in 247 languages account for 29% of the collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>The State Public Historical Library, founded in 1863, is the largest library specialising in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_history" title="Russian history">Russian history</a>. Its collection contains four million items in 112 languages (including 47 languages of the former USSR), mostly on Russian and world history, <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Numismatics" title="Numismatics">numismatics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">history of science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>In regard to primary and secondary education, in 2011, <a href="/wiki/Clifford_J._Levy" title="Clifford J. Levy">Clifford J. Levy</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> wrote, "Moscow has some strong public schools, but the system as a whole is dispiriting, in part because it is being corroded by the corruption that is a post-Soviet scourge. Parents often pay bribes to get their children admitted to better public schools. There are additional payoffs for good grades."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levy1_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levy1-187">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Moscow" title="Transportation in Moscow">Transportation in Moscow</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1730" data-file-width="1330" decoding="async" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg/220px-Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg/330px-Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg/440px-Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_metro_ring_railway_map_en_sb_future.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a> route map with planned stations</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3732" data-file-width="5740" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg/240px-Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg/360px-Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg/480px-Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_MayakovskayaMetroStation_0943.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mayakovskaya_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Mayakovskaya (Moscow Metro)">Mayakovskaya</a> station opened in 1938.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a> system is famous for its art, <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaics</a>, and ornate <a href="/wiki/Chandelier" title="Chandelier">chandeliers</a>. It started operation in 1935 and immediately became the centrepiece of the transportation system. More than that it was a Stalinist device to awe and reward the populace, and give them an appreciation of Soviet realist art. It became the prototype for future Soviet large-scale technologies. <a href="/wiki/Lazar_Kaganovich" title="Lazar Kaganovich">Lazar Kaganovich</a> was in charge; he designed the subway so that citizens would absorb the values and ethos of Stalinist civilisation as they rode. The artwork of the 13 original stations became nationally and internationally famous. For example, the Sverdlov Square subway station featured porcelain bas-reliefs depicting the daily life of the Soviet peoples, and the bas-reliefs at the Dynamo Stadium sports complex glorified sports and the physical prowess of the powerful new "Homo Sovieticus" (Soviet man).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>The metro was touted as the symbol of the new social order—a sort of Communist cathedral of engineering modernity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Soviet workers did the labour and the artwork, but the main engineering designs, routes, and construction plans were handled by specialists recruited from the London Underground. The Britons called for tunneling instead of the "cut-and-cover" technique, the use of escalators instead of lifts, and designed the routes and the rolling stock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The paranoia of Stalin and the NKVD was evident when the secret police arrested numerous British engineers for espionage—that is for gaining an in-depth knowledge of the city's physical layout. Engineers for the Metropolitan Vickers Electrical Company were given a show trial and deported in 1933, ending the role of British business in the USSR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>
</p><p>Today, the Moscow Metro comprises twelve lines, mostly underground with a total of 203 stations. The Metro is one of the deepest subway systems in the world; for instance, the <a href="/wiki/Park_Pobedy_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Park Pobedy (Moscow Metro)">Park Pobedy</a> station, completed in 2003, at 84 metres (276 ft) underground, has the longest escalators in Europe. The Moscow Metro is the busiest metro system in Europe, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_systems_by_annual_passenger_rides" title="Metro systems by annual passenger rides">one of the world's busiest</a> metro systems, serving about ten million passengers daily (300,000,000 people every month).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metro_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-metro-192">[192]</a></sup> Facing serious transportation problems, Moscow has plans for expanding its Metro. In 2016, the authorities launched a <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Circle" title="Moscow Central Circle">new circle metro railway</a> that contributed to solving transportation issues, namely daily congestion at Koltsevaya Line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the treatment of Metro stations as possible canvas for art, characterized by the fact that workers of Moscow would get to see them every day, many Stalin-era metro stations were built in different "custom" designs (where each station's design would be, initially, a massive installation on a certain theme. For example, <a href="/wiki/Elektrozavodskaya_(Arbatsko%E2%80%93Pokrovskaya_line)" title="Elektrozavodskaya (Arbatsko–Pokrovskaya line)">Elektrozavodskaya</a> station was themed solely after nearby lightbulb factory and ceramic ribbed lightbulb sockets);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> the tradition of "Grand Designs" and, basically, decorating metro stations as single-themed installations, was restored in late 1979.
</p><p>More recently, Moscow mayor Sergei Sobyanin has introduced comforts ranging from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WiFi" title="WiFi">WiFi</a> and <a href="/wiki/USB" title="USB">USB</a> ports and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Pay" title="Apple Pay">Apple Pay</a> — while opening new stations at a breakneck pace. Moscow's metro is one of the world's busiest, handling 2.6 billion passengers in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Russian capital, there are over 21.5 thousand Wi-Fi access points, in student dormitories, in parks, cultural and sports institutions, and within the Garden Ring and the Third Transport Ring. From September 2020 to August 2021, 1,700 new access points to urban Wi-Fi were launched in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The structure of the Wi-Fi network allows citizens to use the Internet without re-authorization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monorail">Monorail</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2958" data-file-width="3677" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg/220px-Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg/330px-Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg/440px-Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monorail_Moskau_-_Einfahrt_in_Station_Telezentrum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two trains of the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Monorail" title="Moscow Monorail">Moscow Monorail</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Monorail" title="Moscow Monorail">Moscow Monorail</a></div>
<p>The Moscow Metro operates a short <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Monorail" title="Moscow Monorail">monorail line</a> (line 13). The line connects <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timiryazevskaya_(Serpukhovsko-Timiryazevskaya_Line)" title="Timiryazevskaya (Serpukhovsko-Timiryazevskaya Line)">Timiryazevskaya</a> metro station and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulitsa_Sergeya_Eisensteina" title="Ulitsa Sergeya Eisensteina">Ulitsa Sergeya Eisensteina</a>, passing close to <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_of_Achievements_of_National_Economy" title="Exhibition of Achievements of National Economy">VDNH</a> (and Line 6 Metro station "V.D.N.Kh."). The line opened in 2004. It accepts overgound interchanges, no additional fare is needed if a ride was spent at Moscow Metro within previous 90 minutes.
</p>
<h3><span id="Bus.2C_trolleybus_and_electric_bus"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus,_trolleybus_and_electric_bus">Bus, trolleybus and electric bus</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_buses_in_Moscow" title="Electric buses in Moscow">Electric buses in Moscow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D0%92%D1%8B%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_500-%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8E_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B5_%2809%29.jpg/440px-%D0%92%D1%8B%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_500-%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8E_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B5_%2809%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D1%8B%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_500-%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8E_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B5_(09).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Moscow has the <a href="/wiki/Electric_buses_in_Moscow" title="Electric buses in Moscow">largest fleet of electric buses</a> in Europe, with 500 operating as of October 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trolleybus_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trolleybus-198">[198]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>As Metro stations outside the city center are far apart in comparison to other cities, up to 4 kilometres (2.5 mi), a bus network radiates from each station to the surrounding residential zones. Moscow has a bus terminal for long-range and intercity passenger buses (<a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Bus_Terminal" title="Moscow Central Bus Terminal">Central Bus Terminal</a>) with a daily turnover of about 25 thousand passengers serving about 40% of long-range bus routes in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>Every major street in the city is served by at least one bus route. Many of these routes are doubled by a <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> route and have trolley wires over them.
</p><p>With the total line length of almost 600 kilometres (370 miles) of a single wire, 8 depots, 104 routes, and 1740 vehicles, the Moscow trolleybus system was the <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus_usage_by_country" title="Trolleybus usage by country">largest in the world</a>. But municipal authority, headed by Sergey Sobyanin, began to destroy the trolleybus system in Moscow in 2014 due the planned replacement of trolleybuses by electric buses. In 2018 Moscow trolleybus system has only 4 depots and dozens of kilometers of unused wires. Almost all trolleybus wires inside Garden Ring (Sadovoe Koltso) were cut in 2016–2017 due to the reconstruction of central streets ("Moya Ulitsa"). Opened on November 15, 1933, it is also the world's 6th oldest operating trolleybus system.
</p><p>In 2018 the vehicle companies <a href="/wiki/Kamaz" title="Kamaz">Kamaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/GAZ" title="GAZ">GAZ</a> have won the <a href="/wiki/Mosgortrans" title="Mosgortrans">Mosgortrans</a> tender for delivering 200 <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">electric buses</a> and 62 ultra-fast charging stations to the city transport system. The manufacturers will be responsible for the quality and reliable operation of the buses and charging stations for the next 15 years. The city will be procuring only electric buses as of 2021, replacing the diesel bus fleet gradually. According to expectations, Moscow will become the leader amongst the European cities in terms of electric and gas fuel share in public transport by 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>All bus stations and terminals of Moscow are now connected to free Wi-Fi. One may use it in international bus stations Salaryevo, South Gate and North Gate, and in bus terminals Varshavskaya and Orekhovo. As much as 48 hot spots were installed there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_cable_car">Moscow cable car</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg/220px-Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg/330px-Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg/440px-Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Cable_Car.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cable cars passing across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River" title="Moskva River">Moskva River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River_cable_car" title="Moskva River cable car">Moskva River cable car</a></div>
<p>On November 26, 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Moscow" title="Mayor of Moscow">mayor of Moscow</a> <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Sobyanin" title="Sergey Sobyanin">Sergey Sobyanin</a> took part in the ceremony to open the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River_cable_car" title="Moskva River cable car">cable car</a> above the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River" title="Moskva River">Moskva River</a>. The cable car will connect the <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Olympic_Complex" title="Luzhniki Olympic Complex">Luzhniki sports complex</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sparrow_Hills" title="Sparrow Hills">Sparrow Hills</a> and Kosygin Street.
</p><p>The journey from the well-known viewpoint on Vorobyovy Gory to <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a> will last for five minutes instead of 20 minutes that one would have to spend on the same journey by car. The cable car will work every day from 11 a.m. till 11 p.m.
</p><p>The cable car is 720 meters (2,360 ft) long. It was built to transport 1,600 passengers per hour in all weathers. There are 35 closed capsules designed by Porsche Design Studio to transport passengers. The booths are equipped with media screens, LED lights, hooks for bikes, skis, and snowboards. Passengers will also be able to use audio guides in English, German, Chinese and Russian.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Moscow" title="Trams in Moscow">Trams in Moscow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3483" data-file-width="6192" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg/220px-Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg/330px-Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg/440px-Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_TverZastava_Vityaz_asv2018-09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Vityaz-M tram passing by the <a href="/wiki/Tverskaya_Zastava_Square" title="Tverskaya Zastava Square">Tverskaya Zastava Square</a></div></div></div>
<p>Moscow has an extensive tram system, which first opened in 1899.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The newest line was built in 1984. Its daily usage by Muscovites is low, making up for approximately 5% of trips because many vital connections in the network have been withdrawn. Trams still remain important in some districts as feeders to Metro stations. The trams also provide important cross-links between metro lines, for example between <a href="/wiki/Universitet_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Universitet (Moscow Metro)">Universitet station</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sokolnicheskaya_Line" title="Sokolnicheskaya Line">Sokolnicheskaya Line</a> (#1 red line) and <a href="/wiki/Profsoyuznaya_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Profsoyuznaya (Moscow Metro)">Profsoyuznaya station</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaluzhsko-Rizhskaya_Line" title="Kaluzhsko-Rizhskaya Line">Kaluzhsko-Rizhskaya Line</a> (#6 orange line) or between <a href="/wiki/Voykovskaya_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Voykovskaya (Moscow Metro)">Voykovskaya</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strogino_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Strogino (Moscow Metro)">Strogino</a>. Some routes used to connect downtown with sleep districts, like route 3.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3750" data-file-width="3750" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg/220px-Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg/330px-Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg/440px-Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_tram_map_2022-04.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tram map of Moscow</div></div></div>
<p>There are three tram networks in the city:
</p>
<ul><li>Krasnopresnenskoye depot network with the westernmost point at Strogino (depot location) and the easternmost point near platform Dmitrovskaya. This network became separated in 1973, but until 1997 it could easily have been reconnected by about one kilometre (fifty chains) of track and three switches. The network has the highest usage in Moscow and no weak points based on turnover except to-depot lane (passengers serviced by bus) and tram ring at Dmitrovskaya (because now it is neither a normal transfer point nor a repair terminal).</li>
<li>The Apakov depot services the south-western part from the Varshavsky lane – Simferopolsky boulevard in the east to the Universitet station in the west and Boulevard lane at the center. This network is connected only by the four-way Dubininskaya and Kozhevnicheskaya streets. A second connection by Vostochnaya (Eastern) street was withdrawn in 1987 due to a fire at the Dinamo plant and has not been recovered, and remains lost (Avtozavodsky bridge) at 1992. The network may be serviced anyway by another depot (now route 35, 38).</li>
<li>Main three depot networks with railway gate and tram-repair plant.</li></ul>
<p>In addition, tram advocates have suggested that the new rapid transit services (metro to City, Butovo light metro, Monorail) would be more effective as at-grade tram lines and that the problems with trams are only due to poor management and operation, not the technical properties of trams. New tram models have been developed for the Moscow network despite the lack of expansion.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span></h3>
<p>Commercial taxi services and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_taxi" title="Route taxi">route taxis</a> are in widespread use. In the mid-2010s, service platforms such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yandex.Taxi" title="Yandex.Taxi">Yandex.Taxi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uber" title="Uber">Uber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gett" title="Gett">Gett</a> displaced many private drivers and small service providers and were in 2015 servicing more than 50% of all taxi orders in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>Russian tech firm Yandex is testing self-driving taxis in Moscow. Yandex's fleet of around 170 driverless cars has travelled more than 14 million kilometres. Robotaxis will available through the company's Yandex.Go application in Yasenevo district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span></h3>

terminal situated there: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Passazhirskaya_railway_station" title="Moscow Passazhirskaya railway station">Leningradsky</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" Kazanskaya railway station">Kazansky</a></div></div></div><p> Several train stations serve the city. Moscow's ten rail terminals (or <span title="Russian-language romanization"><i lang="ru-Latn">vokzals</i></span>) are:
</p><ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belorussky_Rail_Terminal" title="Belorussky Rail Terminal">Belorussky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazansky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kazansky Rail Terminal">Kazansky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kiyevsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kiyevsky Rail Terminal">Kiyevsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kursky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kursky Rail Terminal">Kursky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningradsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Leningradsky Rail Terminal">Leningradsky Rail Terminal</a></li>

<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savyolovsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Savyolovsky Rail Terminal">Savyolovsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yaroslavsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Yaroslavsky Rail Terminal">Yaroslavsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostochny_Railway_Terminal_(Moscow)" title="Vostochny Railway Terminal (Moscow)">Vostochny railway Terminal</a></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bullet-Train.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bullet-Train.jpg/220px-Bullet-Train.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bullet-Train.jpg/330px-Bullet-Train.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bullet-Train.jpg/440px-Bullet-Train.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bullet-Train.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The high-speed <a href="/wiki/Sapsan" title="Sapsan">Sapsan</a> train links Moscow with <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The terminals are located close to the city center, along with the metro ringline 5 or close to it, and connect to a metro line to the centre of town. Each station handles trains from different parts of Europe and Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mostimestrain_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-mostimestrain-206">[206]</a></sup> There are many smaller railway stations in Moscow. As train tickets are cheap, they are the preferred mode of travel for Russians, especially when departing to Saint Petersburg, Russia's second-largest city. Moscow is the western terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>, which traverses nearly 9,300 kilometres (5,800 mi) of Russian territory to <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> coast.
</p><p>Suburbs and satellite cities are connected by commuter <a href="/wiki/Elektrichka" title="Elektrichka">elektrichka</a> (electric rail) network. Elektrichkas depart from each of these terminals to the nearby (up to 140 km or 87 mi) large railway stations.
</p><p>During the 2010s, the <a href="/wiki/Little_Ring_of_the_Moscow_Railway" title="Little Ring of the Moscow Railway">Little Ring of the Moscow Railway</a> was converted to be used for frequent passenger service; it is fully integrated with Moscow Metro; the passenger service started on September 10, 2016. A connecting railway line on the North side of the town connects Belorussky terminal with other railway lines. This is used by some suburban trains.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_Central_Circle">Moscow Central Circle</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg/220px-MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg/330px-MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg/440px-MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MCC_12LUZH_7041_PLAT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Lastochka" train on "<a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_(Moscow_Central_Circle)" title="Luzhniki (Moscow Central Circle)">Luzhniki</a>" station (Line 14)</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Little_Ring_of_the_Moscow_Railway" title="Little Ring of the Moscow Railway">Moskovskaya Okruzhnaya Zheleznaya Doroga</a> formed a ring around the now-downtown Moscow since 1903, but only served as a non-electrified, fueled locomotive-only railway prior to reconstruction into MCC in 2010's.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Circle" title="Moscow Central Circle">Moscow Central Circle</a> is a 54-kilometre-long (34 mi) <a href="/wiki/Urban_rail_transit" title="Urban rail transit">urban-metro railway</a> orbital line that encircles historical Moscow. It was built alongside <a href="/wiki/Little_Ring_of_the_Moscow_Railway" title="Little Ring of the Moscow Railway">Little Ring of the Moscow Railway</a>, taking some of its tracks into itself as well. M.C.C. was opened for passenger use on September 10, 2016. MOZD is integrated as "Line 14 of Moscow Metro", and, while using railway-sized trains, can be perceived as "S-train-design circle line".
</p><p>The line is operated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Government" title="Moscow Government">Moscow Government</a> owned company MKZD through the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Federal Government</a> owned <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railways" title="Russian Railways">Russian Railways</a> selected as the operation subcontractor. The track infrastructure and most platforms are owned by Russian Railways, while MKZD owns most station buildings. However, in <i>S-bahn</i> way, Moscow unified tickets "Ediniiy" and "Troika" are accepted by MCC stations. There is one zero-fee interchange for any ticket used on Moscow Metro station less than 90 minutes before entering an MCC station (and vice versa: a passenger of MCC gets 1 free interchange to Moscow Metro within 90 minutes after entering MCC station)
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_Central_Diameters">Moscow Central Diameters</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_(platform_4).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_%28platform_4%29.jpg/220px-EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_%28platform_4%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_%28platform_4%29.jpg/330px-EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_%28platform_4%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_%28platform_4%29.jpg/440px-EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_%28platform_4%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EG2Tv_arrives_to_Belorussky_rail_terminal_(platform_4).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Ivolga_(train)" title="Ivolga (train)">EG2Tv</a> train arriving at the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Belorussky_railway_station" title="Moscow Belorussky railway station">Moscow Belorussky railway station</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2240" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg/220px-Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg/330px-Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg/440px-Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_Central_Diameters_-_passenger_scheme1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Diameters" title="Moscow Central Diameters">Moscow Central Diameters</a></div></div></div>
<p>Another system, which forms "genuine <i>S-Bahn</i>" as in "suburbia-city-suburbia"-designed railway, is the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Diameters" title="Moscow Central Diameters">Moscow Central Diameters</a>, a pass-through railways system, created by constructing bypasses from "vokzals" final stations (e.g. by avoiding the central stations of already existing Moscow Railway, used for both intercity and urban-suburban travel before)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> and forming a train line across Moscow's centre.
</p><p>Out of 5 projected lines, the first 2 lines were completed and launched on 2019-11-21 (e.g. November 21, 2019).
</p><p>While using the same rails as "regular" suburban trains to vokzals, MCD trains ("<i><a href="/wiki/Ivolga_(train)" title="Ivolga (train)">Ivolga</a></i>" model) got distinguishing features (shape; red cabin, different windows, lesser amount of seats; big red "MЦΔ" train logo).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A2%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%97%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0_(%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%85%D1%83).jpg"><img
