1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A2%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%97%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0_%28%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%85%D1%83%29.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A2%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%97%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0_%28%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%85%D1%83%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A2%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%97%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B0_(%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%85%D1%83).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Intersection at <a href="/wiki/Tverskaya_Zastava_Square" title="Tverskaya Zastava Square">Tverskaya Zastava Square</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are over 2.6 million cars in the city daily. Recent years have seen growth in the number of cars, which have caused traffic jams and lack of parking space to become major problems.
</p><p>The Moscow Ring Road (MKAD), along with the <a href="/wiki/Third_Ring_Road_(Moscow)" title="Third Ring Road (Moscow)">Third Transport Ring</a> and the canceled Fourth Transport Ring, is one of only three freeways that run within Moscow city limits. Several other roadway systems form <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concentric_circles" title="Concentric circles">concentric circles</a> around the city.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span></h3>
<p>There are five primary commercial airports serving Moscow: <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">Sheremetyevo</a> (SVO), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domodedovo_International_Airport" title="Domodedovo International Airport">Domodedovo</a> (DME), <a href="/wiki/Vnukovo_International_Airport" title="Vnukovo International Airport">Vnukovo</a> (VKO), <a href="/wiki/Zhukovsky_International_Airport" title="Zhukovsky International Airport">Zhukovsky</a> (ZIA), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ostafyevo_International_Airport" title="Ostafyevo International Airport">Ostafyevo</a> (OSF).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="846" data-file-width="1158" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheremetyevo, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Russia" title="List of the busiest airports in Russia">busiest airport in Russia</a>, is ranked as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">second-busiest airport</a> in Europe.</div></div></div>
<p>Sheremetyevo International Airport is the most globally connected, handling 60% of all international flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4airports_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-4airports-208">[208]</a></sup> It is also a home to all <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> members, and the main hub for <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a> (itself a member of SkyTeam). Domodedovo International Airport is the leading airport in Russia in terms of passenger throughput and is the primary gateway to long-haul domestic and CIS destinations and its international traffic rivals Sheremetyevo. It is a hub for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S7_airlines" title="S7 airlines">S7 airlines</a>, and most of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OneWorld" title="OneWorld">OneWorld</a> and <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> members use Domodedovo as their international hub. Vnukovo International Airport handles flights of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> and others. Ostafyevo International Airport caters primarily to business aviation.
</p><p>Moscow's airports vary in distances from the MKAD beltway: Domodedovo is the farthest at 22 km (14 mi); Vnukovo is 11 km (7 mi); Sheremetyevo is 10 km (6 mi); and Ostafievo, the nearest, is about 8 kilometres (5.0 mi) from MKAD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4airports_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-4airports-208">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are a number of smaller airports close to Moscow (19 in Moscow Oblast) such as <a href="/wiki/Myachkovo_Airport" title="Myachkovo Airport">Myachkovo Airport</a>, that are intended for private aircraft, helicopters and charters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span></h3>
<p>Moscow has two passenger terminals, (<a href="/wiki/South_River_Terminal" title="South River Terminal">South River Terminal</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_River_Terminal" title="North River Terminal">North River Terminal</a> or Rechnoy vokzal), on the river and regular ship routes and cruises along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskva_River" title="Moskva River">Moskva</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oka_River" title="Oka River">Oka</a> rivers, which are used mostly for entertainment. The <a href="/wiki/North_River_Terminal" title="North River Terminal">North River Terminal</a>, built in 1937, is the main hub for long-range river routes. There are three freight ports serving Moscow.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sharing_system">Sharing system</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Carsharing_in_Moscow" title="Carsharing in Moscow">Carsharing in Moscow</a></div>

title="Enlarge"></a></div>As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Moscow has the <a href="/wiki/Carsharing_in_Moscow" title="Carsharing in Moscow">largest fleet of carsharing vehicles</a> in the world, with more than 30,000 cars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carsharing_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carsharing-210">[210]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Moscow has different vehicle sharing options that are sponsored by the local government. There are several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Car_sharing" title="Car sharing">car sharing</a> companies which are in charge of providing cars to the population. To drive the automobiles, the user has to book them through the app of the owning company. In 2018 the mayor <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Sobyanin" title="Sergey Sobyanin">Sergey Sobyanin</a> said Moscow's car sharing system has become the biggest in Europe in terms of vehicle fleet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> Every day about 25,000 people use this service. In the end of the same year Moscow carsharing became the second in the world in therms of fleet with 16.5K available vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Another sharing system is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bike_sharing" title="Bike sharing">bike sharing</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Velobike" title="Velobike">Velobike</a></i>) of a fleet formed by 3000 traditional and electrical bicycles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> The <i>Delisamokat</i> is a new sharing service that provides electrical scooters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> There are companies that provide different vehicles to the population in proximity to Moscow's big parks.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_development">Future development</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_(2020).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="614" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%282020%29.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%282020%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%282020%29.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%282020%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%282020%29.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%282020%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B2_%D0%9C%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_(2020).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2020 development concept of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">Moscow International Business Center</a> and its adjacent territory implies the construction of even more skyscrapers during the period of 2020–2027.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 1992, the Moscow government began planning a projected new part of central Moscow, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">Moscow International Business Center</a>, with the goal of creating a zone, the first in Russia, and in all of Eastern Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> that will combine business activity, living space and entertainment. Situated in <a href="/wiki/Presnensky_District" title="Presnensky District">Presnensky District</a> and located at the Third Ring, the Moscow City area is under intense development. The construction of the MIBC takes place on the Krasnopresnenskaya embankment. The whole project takes up to one square kilometre (250 acres). The area is the only spot in downtown Moscow that can accommodate a project of this magnitude. Today, most of the buildings there are old factories and industrial complexes.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Federation_Tower" title="Federation Tower">Federation Tower</a>, completed in 2016, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Europe" title="List of tallest buildings in Europe">second-tallest building in Europe</a>. It is planned to include a <a href="/wiki/Water_park" title="Water park">water park</a> and other recreational facilities; business, office, entertainment, and residential buildings, a transport network and a <a href="/wiki/City_Hall_and_City_Duma" title="City Hall and City Duma">new site for the Moscow government</a>. The construction of four new metro stations in the territory has been completed, two of which have opened and two others are reserved for future metro lines crossing MIBC, some additional stations were planned. 
</p>
<ul><li>A rail shuttle service, directly connecting <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">MIBC</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">Sheremetyevo International Airport</a> is also planned.</li></ul>
<p>Major thoroughfares through MIBC are the <a href="/wiki/Third_Ring_Road_(Moscow)" title="Third Ring Road (Moscow)">Third Ring</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kutuzovsky_Prospekt" title="Kutuzovsky Prospekt">Kutuzovsky Prospekt</a>.
</p><p>Three metro stations were initially planned for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filyovskaya_Line" title="Filyovskaya Line">Filyovskaya Line</a>. The station Delovoi Tsentr opened in 2005 and was later renamed <a href="/wiki/Vystavochnaya" title="Vystavochnaya">Vystavochnaya</a> in 2009. The branch extended to the <a href="/wiki/Mezhdunarodnaya_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Mezhdunarodnaya (Moscow Metro)">Mezhdunarodnaya</a> station in 2006, and all work on the third station, Dorogomilovskaya (between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kiyevskaya_(Filyovskaya)" title="Kiyevskaya (Filyovskaya)">Kiyevskaya</a> and Delovoi Tsentr), has been postponed. There are plans to extend the branch as far as the <a href="/wiki/Savyolovskaya_(Serpukhovsko%E2%80%93Timiryazevskaya_line)" title="Savyolovskaya (Serpukhovsko–Timiryazevskaya line)">Savyolovskaya</a> station, on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serpukhovsko-Timiryazevskaya_Line" title="Serpukhovsko-Timiryazevskaya Line">Serpukhovsko-Timiryazevskaya Line</a>. Line 4 of Moscow Metro had the longest time intervals between train arrivals (approximately 8 minutes for Mezhdunarodnaya and Vystavochnaya branch of line 4) throughout the 2010s. However, Vystavochnaya has been expanded with Line 8A platforms (segment of future Line 11), and Mezhdunarodnaya has been upgraded with <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Circle" title="Moscow Central Circle">line 14</a> platform.
</p><p>The cellphone service provider MTS announced on March 5, 2021, that they would begin the country's first pilot <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">5G</a> network in Moscow. 14 hotspots were positioned across the city's main tourist attractions, including Lubyanka Square near Red Square, the Moscow City financial district and the VDNKh exhibition center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_of_Russia" title="Media of Russia">Media of Russia</a></div>
<p>Moscow is home to nearly all of Russia's nationwide <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Russia" title="Television in Russia">television networks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio stations</a>, newspapers, and magazines.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Russia" title="List of newspapers in Russia">List of newspapers in Russia</a></div>
<p>English-language media include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Moscow_Times" title="The Moscow Times">The Moscow Times</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_News" title="Moscow News">Moscow News</a></i>, which are, respectively, the largest<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> and oldest English-language weekly newspapers in all of Russia. <i><a href="/wiki/Kommersant" title="Kommersant">Kommersant</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vedomosti" title="Vedomosti">Vedomosti</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Novaya_Gazeta" title="Novaya Gazeta">Novaya Gazeta</a></i> are Russian-language media headquartered in Moscow. <i>Kommersant</i> and <i>Vedomosti</i> are among the country's leading and oldest Russian-language business newspapers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TV_and_radio">TV and radio</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Russia" title="Television in Russia">Television in Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg/220px-2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg/330px-2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg/440px-2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2019-07-28-3422-Moscow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Television_and_Radio_Broadcasting_Network" title="Russian Television and Radio Broadcasting Network">RTRN</a> building</div></div></div>
<p>Other media in Moscow include the <i><a href="/wiki/Echo_of_Moscow" title="Echo of Moscow">Echo of Moscow</a></i>, the first Soviet and Russian private news radio and information agency, and <a href="/wiki/NTV_(Russia)" title="NTV (Russia)">NTV</a>, one of the first privately owned Russian television stations. The total number of radio stations in Moscow in the FM band is near 50.
</p><p><b>Moscow television networks:</b>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Moscow" title="List of people from Moscow">List of people from Moscow</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Moscow" title="Category:People from Moscow">Category:People from Moscow</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 130.66666666667px"><div style="width: 130.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 128.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_(Orest_Kiprensky,_1827).PNG" title="Alexander Pushkin, the founder of modern Russian literature was born in Moscow in 1799."><img alt="Alexander Pushkin, the founder of modern Russian literature was born in Moscow in 1799." data-file-height="1472" data-file-width="1263" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_%28Orest_Kiprensky%2C_1827%29.PNG/193px-Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_%28Orest_Kiprensky%2C_1827%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_%28Orest_Kiprensky%2C_1827%29.PNG/290px-Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_%28Orest_Kiprensky%2C_1827%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_%28Orest_Kiprensky%2C_1827%29.PNG/386px-Portrait_of_Alexander_Pushkin_%28Orest_Kiprensky%2C_1827%29.PNG 2x" width="129"/></a></div></div>

<p><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a>, the founder of modern <a href="/wiki/Russian_literature" title="Russian literature">Russian literature</a> was born in Moscow in 1799.
</p>
</div>

<p>Moscow has cooperation agreements with:

<li id="cite_note-MoscowO-150"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-MoscowO_150-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Article 24 of the Charter of Moscow Oblast, the government bodies of the oblast are located in the city of Moscow and throughout the territory of Moscow Oblast. However, Moscow is not officially named the administrative centre of the oblast.</span>
</li>
